# Muse Migration Plan

Source baseline: Reactor has 31 Gradle modules under `/modules` plus the root `app` bootstrap project.

Current Muse baseline:
- Packages: 23
- Apps: 3
- Rust crates: 1
- Verified gate: `pnpm check`
- Branch state: verify with `git status -sb` before pushing or merging
- Route parity is currently tracked separately from DB/state parity.

## Current Count

| Bucket | Count | Meaning |
| --- | ---: | --- |
| Reactor source modules with Muse landing zones | 31 | Every `modules/*` source module has a package or API target |
| Reactor included projects with Muse landing zones | 32 | `app` plus all 31 source modules are mapped |
| Cross-cutting compatibility areas | 4 | Context, response filtering, hooks, and multi-agent behavior are tracked as capabilities, not Reactor source modules |
| HTTP route parity | 255 / 255 | Every Reactor controller route under `app` and `modules` is registered in Muse |
| DB table parity | 52 / 52 | Every Reactor persistent table name has a Muse migration target; store wiring is still being migrated |
| Functionally exercised source modules | 31 | Core behavior exists and is covered by package/API tests |
| Deep-hardening areas still open | 4 | Response filters, Slack behavior, hook/context behavior, and DB-backed state parity remain open |
| Remaining unmapped modules | 0 | No source module is without a target |

## Completed Migration Areas

| Reactor module | Muse target | Current status |
| --- | --- | --- |
| `app` | `apps/api` | Runtime bootstrap, environment assembly, Fastify server entrypoint |
| `agent` | `packages/agent-core` | ReAct loop, tool execution, streaming, guards, hooks, cache, RAG, history |
| `api` | `apps/api` | Chat, SSE chat, auth, settings, agent specs, history, MCP, scheduler, quality routes |
| `admin` | `apps/api`, `packages/runtime-state`, `packages/db` | Metrics, cache, alert, cost, SLO, tenant ops |
| `approval` | `packages/policy`, `packages/runtime-state` | Approval policies and pending approval stores exist |
| `auth` | `packages/auth`, `apps/api`, `packages/db` | JWT auth, password hashing, DB/in-memory user store, DB/in-memory revocation, guard, rate limiting |
| `autoconfigure` | `packages/autoconfigure` | Environment-driven runtime assembly and DB-backed store selection exist |
| `cache` | `packages/cache` | Response cache, scope fingerprint, TTL invalidation, prompt-cache metadata, stats |
| `common` | `packages/shared` | Shared IDs, JSON, and common value types exist |
| `core` | `apps/api`, `packages/autoconfigure` | Fastify bootstrap and runtime assembly replace Spring Boot core |
| `eval` | `packages/eval`, `apps/api` | Eval case model, judges, runner, summaries, and admin API exist |
| `guard` | `packages/policy`, `packages/agent-core` | Input/output guards and fail-close runtime integration exist |
| `hook` | `packages/agent-core`, `packages/runtime-state` | Registry callbacks, tool lifecycle hooks, and hook trace stores exist |
| `hook-integrations` | `packages/integrations` | Lifecycle webhook dispatch and HMAC signing primitives exist |
| `intent` | `packages/agent-specs` | Agent specs, resolver, registry, and Kysely mapping exist |
| `memory` | `packages/memory`, `packages/runtime-state` | Context trimming, compaction summaries, checkpoints, run history, and stores exist |
| `mcp` | `packages/mcp`, `apps/api` | SDK transports, health checks, reconnect, and management APIs exist |
| `model-routing` | `packages/model` | Provider registry, prefix routing, OpenAI-compatible, OpenAI, OpenRouter, Ollama, Anthropic, and Gemini adapters exist |
| `observability` | `packages/observability`, `packages/runtime-state`, `packages/db` | Tracing, persisted trace events, metrics, and history stores exist |
| `persistence-schema` | `packages/db` | Kysely schema covers runtime, scheduler, MCP, and admin state |
| `promptlab` | `packages/promptlab`, `apps/api` | Prompt variants, experiments, runner, ranking, and admin API exist |
| `prompts` | `packages/prompts` | Prompt assembly, response format instructions, and cache boundary helpers exist |
| `rag` | `packages/rag` | Chunking, BM25/RRF retrieval, reranking, context building, and in-memory corpus exist |
| `resilience` | `packages/resilience` | Circuit breaker registry, retry, timeout, and model fallback primitives exist |
| `runtime-settings` | `packages/runtime-settings`, `apps/api` | Runtime settings service/store and API surface exist |
| `scheduler` | `packages/scheduler`, `apps/api` | CRUD, execution records, cron, and scheduler locks exist |
| `slack` | `packages/integrations`, `apps/api` | Signed Events API dispatch plus thread replies, slash-command channel/thread posting, interaction dispatch, persisted response tracking and feedback metadata, response_url fallback, and Slack mrkdwn response formatting exist |
| `tool` | `packages/tools` | Tool registry, executor, sanitizer, and approval path exist |
| `web` | `apps/api`, `apps/web` | HTTP/SSE run endpoints, typed error surfaces, and initial Vite/React operator UI exist |

## Cross-Cutting Compatibility Areas

These are not Reactor Gradle modules, but they are kept as explicit migration checks because they affect parity across
multiple source modules.

| Area | Muse target | Current status |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Context handling | `packages/memory`, `packages/agent-core` | Context trimming, pinned-entity compaction summaries, and assistant/tool message-pair handling exist |
| Response filtering | `packages/policy`, `packages/agent-core` | Output guards, verified-source rendering, source/structured filters, markdown/sanitized-text cleanup, greeting/lure stripping, fabrication refusal, policy-prior warning, max-length truncation, Slack ID masking, internal brand masking, tool-result quality audit, response-count injection/consistency, zero-result overclaim cleanup, and release-risk data-gap cleanup exist |
| Hook lifecycle | `packages/agent-core`, `packages/runtime-state`, `packages/integrations` | Agent/tool hook callbacks, trace persistence, and webhook signing exist |
| Multi-agent orchestration | `packages/multi-agent` | Supervisor, worker selection, fallback, sequential/parallel delegation, and handoff trace primitives exist |

## Remaining Deep-Hardening Areas

No known source module remains unmapped.
The remaining checks are cross-module behavior parity checks that should be closed before calling the migration
fully done:

1. Response filters: compare Reactor's verified-source extractor edge cases against Muse extraction
   (nested URL fields, synthesized source directories, and source relevance filtering still need broader parity tests).
2. Slack behavior: verify Socket Mode behavior beyond the HTTP webhook, threaded response tracking, and feedback-store wiring now covered in Muse packages.
3. Hook/context behavior: verify message-pair integrity under broader runtime smoke tests.
4. DB-backed state parity: move remaining Reactor-compatible state out of process-local compatibility Maps and into Kysely-backed stores.

Latest route parity check: `REACTOR_SOURCE_DIR=<local-reactor-path> pnpm verify:reactor-routes` reports 255 Reactor
routes, 369 Muse routes, and 0 missing Reactor routes.

Latest DB parity check: `REACTOR_SOURCE_DIR=<local-reactor-path> pnpm verify:reactor-db` reports 52 Reactor tables,
64 Muse tables, and 0 missing Reactor tables. This is table-name parity only; remaining work is moving compatibility
route state and runtime services onto Kysely-backed stores.

## Recent Completion Notes

- docs (round 185) — voice-mode design doc reconciliation. The doc at `docs/design/voice-mode.md` was labelled `Status: **Proposal** (not started)` but Phases A/B/D/E had actually shipped earlier (`@muse/voice` package with Whisper STT + OpenAI TTS adapters; `/api/voice/{providers,stt,tts}` routes in `apps/api/src/voice-routes.ts`; `<VoicePanel>` Web component in `apps/web/src/ui/App.tsx` with `MediaRecorder` capture + audio playback). Round 185 marks each phase DONE with the concrete file references (so future readers can find the implementations without grep), keeps Phase C (`muse listen` CLI) as the only remaining v1 phase, and writes a **Phase C contract** section sharp enough that the next iter can start coding without re-deciding: `muse listen [--lang ko|en] [--voice <name>] [--output mp3|wav]`, `which sox` boot-check with a clear install hint on miss, `rec -r 16000 -c 1 -t wav -` shell-out for capture, push-to-talk via Enter (silence-detection deferred), pipe through `/api/voice/stt` → `/api/chat` → `/api/voice/tts` → `afplay` / `aplay`, cleanup temp audio + kill sox on Ctrl-C. Test plan: inject the sox / afplay shells via dependencies (mirrors `osascriptPath` pattern from `MacOsCalendarProvider`). macOS mic-permission OS prompt on first run is documented as expected, with the surface-helpful-message-on-permission-denied UX requirement called out. Phase F (wake-word + local Whisper.cpp + Gemini Live) explicitly stays deferred until Phase C lands and real latency/cost data justifies. Doc grew from 161 → 211 lines (+50 lines of concrete next-iter scaffolding). **No code changes** — `pnpm check`, `pnpm smoke:broad` 47/47, `pnpm lint` 0/0 unchanged.

- feat (round 184) — Korean auto-extract prompt (resolves round 166's "extraction prompt is in English only" caveat). Round 166 shipped typed-slot extraction (vetoes / goals) but the system prompt was English-only — Korean-speaking users were getting Gemini-translated semantics with measurable error rates and English-language internal reasoning artifacts in extracted values. New helper `pickAutoExtractSystemPrompt(userPrompt)` in `packages/memory/src/memory-auto-extract.ts`: counts Hangul syllables (U+AC00–U+D7AF) over total characters; ≥30% triggers the new `systemPromptKo`, else falls through to the existing English prompt as the conservative default. The Korean prompt mirrors the English schema (same JSON keys / shape / size limits) but the rules + examples are Korean ("계란 추천 금지", "월요일에는 회의 잡지 마", "Q1까지 Muse 1.0 출시"). Critically, the schema instruction explicitly states "key는 영어로 쓰되 value는 한국어 그대로 둘 수 있다" — keys/ids stay snake_case ASCII so the persistence layer (round 165's JSONB schema) is unchanged, while values stay in the user's native Korean. `runExtraction` calls `pickAutoExtractSystemPrompt` against the user prompt and threads it as the system message. 6 new vitest cases (memory 60 → 66): Hangul-majority message → Korean prompt; English-only → English prompt; mixed-mostly-English → English; ≥30% Hangul threshold honored; empty input → English fallback; integration test confirms `createUserMemoryAutoExtractHook` actually sends the Korean prompt to the model when given Korean input. **Live dogfood with real Gemini API key (env-only, never committed)**: Korean input "참고로 제 배우자 이름은 알렉스이고, 매일 아침 7시에 일어나는 게 좋아요. 그리고 계란은 절대 추천하지 마세요 — 알레르기 있어요." extracted to `facts.spouse_name="알렉스"`, `preferences.wake_up_time="매일 아침 7시에 일어나는 게 좋아요"`, and a typed veto `{id:"no_eggs", value:"계란은 절대 추천하지 마세요", scope:"food"}` — English keys + Korean values + English scope tag, exactly as the prompt instructed. The veto even got the `scope: "food"` cross-language tag right. **Caveat / next iter**: the heuristic is character-based (Hangul ratio), not language-detection — Japanese/Chinese still fall to English. A more comprehensive language switch would need either a third prompt or a small detection model. Auto-extract still off-by-default (`MUSE_USER_MEMORY_AUTO_EXTRACT=true` to enable; extra LLM call/turn). `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 47/47; `pnpm smoke:live` 12/12; `pnpm lint` 0/0.

- feat (round 183) — Context Engineering **step 1.e LLM-summarized fan-in** (upgrade over round 170's deterministic head+tail trim). New `OrchestrationRunOptions.summarizeWorkerOutput?: (workerId, output) => Promise<string>` hook in `@muse/multi-agent`: when set, each worker's `response.output` is replaced with the summarizer's return value BEFORE the deterministic trim (composes cleanly — summarize first, then trim the summary as a belt-and-suspenders guard) and BEFORE the parent concat. Failures (rejected promise, timeout, empty return) fall back to raw output — the orchestrator never blocks on summarization. Tracked `MultiAgentOrchestrationResult.results` stay byte-identical regardless of summarizer usage (same fidelity contract as `maxOutputCharsPerWorker`). The hook is caller-provided so `@muse/multi-agent` stays model-agnostic. `apps/api/src/multi-agent-routes.ts` adds an opt-in `summarize: boolean` body field on `/api/multi-agent/orchestrate` + `/orchestrate/stream`; when `true`, the route builds a Gemini-style summarizer via `createWorkerSummarizer(modelProvider, model)` (uses the runtime's configured `ModelProvider` with a fixed system prompt asking for "single concise summary, 3 sentences max, key facts/decisions/blockers, drop reasoning steps", `maxOutputTokens: 256`, `temperature: 0.2`, 15s timeout via `Promise.race`). `MultiAgentRouteOptions` extended with `modelProvider?: ModelProvider`; `apps/api/src/server.ts` threads `options.modelProvider` through. 3 new vitest cases (multi-agent 39 → 42): summarizer replaces output before fan-in concat (mock summarizer returns `[summary of <id>: <len> chars]`, output contains it, raw is gone, tracked result preserved); summarizer failure falls back to raw output without blocking; summarizer composes with `maxOutputCharsPerWorker` (long summary still capped). **Live dogfood with real Gemini API key (env var only, never committed)**: ran a one-off node script through `GeminiProvider` with a verbose worker emitting 704 chars of multi-step reasoning. Baseline (no summarizer): 704 chars verbatim concat. With summarizer: 290 chars (-58%) — 3-sentence summary preserving all operative facts (LruCache config, max 500, TTL 5min, no-blocker note). Tracked result kept the full 693-char original for trace fidelity. Round 170's deterministic-trim caveat ("the LLM-summarized 'summary fan-in' version is the heavier follow-up") is now resolved. **Caveat / next iter**: per-worker summarizer model override (different worker types might want different summarization strength) deferred — global `summarize: true` flag is the simplest first knob. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 47/47; `pnpm smoke:live` 12/12; `pnpm lint` 0/0.

- feat (round 182) — JARVIS feature: `muse mcp config-doctor` CLI command. Round 175's `config-show` displayed parsed entries; round 182 adds **per-entry validation that doesn't bail on the first malformed entry** — useful when `~/.muse/mcp.json` has multiple problems and the user wants to see them all at once instead of fixing one, re-running, and discovering the next. New helper `diagnoseExternalMcpConfig(raw, source?)` in `packages/autoconfigure/src/external-mcp-config.ts`: parses the outer JSON (still throws `ConfigurationError` on outer JSON failure since that affects every entry), then runs each `mcpServers[name]` through `parseEntry` inside a try-catch. Entries that would have thrown surface as `{ status: "error", findings: ["<message>"] }` with the original error string preserved for actionable debugging. Disabled entries (`disabled: true`) report `{ status: "skipped" }` with a note explaining the entry won't be loaded — distinct from "broken". Successfully-parsed entries report `{ status: "ok", entry, transportType, findings }` where `findings` flags soft issues (non-fatal): currently checks URL validity for streamable/sse transports — `new URL(...)` failure → `findings: ["url is not a valid URL: ..."]`; non-http(s) protocol → `findings: ["url protocol is 'ftp:', expected http: or https:"]`. Companion `diagnoseExternalMcpConfigFile(env)` reads the resolved file and runs the diagnoser; missing file returns `[]` (same as `loadExternalMcpConfig`). New CLI command `muse mcp config-doctor [--json]` runs the diagnosis, prints `<name>\t<STATUS>\t<transport>\t<findings>` per row, exits 1 when any entry has `error` status. 6 new vitest cases in autoconfigure (48 → 56) cover happy/disabled/malformed-URL/non-http-protocol/outer-JSON-fail/missing-mcpServers; 2 new CLI test cases (cli 38 → 40): doctor prints OK rows for valid entries; doctor reports per-entry errors without bailing. Live dogfood verified: ran `node apps/cli/dist/index.js mcp config-doctor` against real `~/.muse/mcp.json` (single filesystem entry → `OK stdio no issues`), then ran against a synthetic broken file (3 entries: 1 valid, 1 missing-transport, 1 bad URL) — all 3 lines printed, exit 1, error count `1 of 3` shown. **Caveat / next iter**: `which <command>` for stdio entries (warn when binary not found on PATH) deferred — needs cross-platform spawn handling; the structural validation in this iter already catches the most common typos. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 47/47; `pnpm lint` 0/0.

- chore (round 181) — promote remaining lint rules to `error`. Round 180 ended with 0 warnings on all rules, so the 6 rules left at `warn` since round 174 (`no-empty`, `no-empty-pattern`, `no-useless-escape`, `no-unsafe-finally`, `no-async-promise-executor`, `no-prototype-builtins`) graduate to `error`. Any new violation now blocks `pnpm lint` exit-0. The codebase passed at the new strictness without any code changes — the round 173 sweep + iter-by-iter discipline since means the codebase is currently free of these patterns. `no-empty` keeps `allowEmptyCatch: true` (the validateTimezone bare-`catch {}` from round 173 stays valid). `.claude/rules/code-style.md` updated to document each rule's reasoning (e.g. why `no-async-promise-executor` matters: it's the classic forgotten-await footgun; why `no-prototype-builtins`: `obj.hasOwnProperty(...)` breaks on null-prototype objects, prefer `Object.hasOwn`). Iter also dogfood-verified: booted server with the real `~/.muse/mcp.json`, asked the LLM to call `muse.notes.save` to write `dogfood-181.md` — file was actually written to disk with the exact requested content (38 bytes), confirming the personal-JARVIS notes flow works end-to-end via real Gemini against the seeded filesystem MCP server. **No real bugs found** in this iter's dogfood pass. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 47/47; `pnpm lint` 0/0 with all 11 rules at `error`.

- refactor (round 180) — big-file decomp continues: extract text-formatting tools from `packages/tools/src/muse-tools.ts` (847 → 606 LOC; combined with round 179 total reduction is 1193 → 606 = -587 LOC over two iters). New `muse-tools-text.ts` (253 LOC) holds the 4 text-domain builders (`createTextStatsTool`, `createSlugifyTool`, `createKvSummarizeTool`, `createMarkdownTableTool`) plus their private helpers (`slugify`, `flattenIntoKv`, `deriveMarkdownTableColumns`, `formatMarkdownTableCell`) and the `KV_SUMMARIZE_MAX_LINES` + `MARKDOWN_TABLE_MAX_ROWS` caps — all co-located with their only call sites. `muse-tools.ts` imports the 4 builders from the new module and uses them in the existing `createMuseTools` factory composition (same public ordering, same returned tool objects). Behavior-preserving: same tools, same schemas, same risk levels, same private constants. The `readOptionalNumber` helper import on `muse-tools.ts` is no longer needed (only used by the slugify tool which moved); lint caught the dead import immediately and forced a clean import line. Personal-JARVIS dogfood unchanged: smoke:live's plan-execute test still passes through real Gemini. **Caveat / next iter**: 7 builders + remaining helpers stay in `muse-tools.ts` — `createMathEvalTool` + `evaluateArithmetic`, `createJsonQueryTool`, `createUrlPartsTool`, `createRegexExtractTool`, `createHashTextTool`, `createCsvParseTool` + `parseCsvRecords`, `createBase64Tool` + `padBase64`. Future iters can extract math+arithmetic, data+encoding, regex+url groups when next reduction is needed. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 47/47; `pnpm smoke:live` 12/12; `pnpm lint` 0/0.

- refactor (round 179) — big-file decomp: extract time/datetime tools from `packages/tools/src/muse-tools.ts` (1193 → 847 LOC, the largest file in the repo). Two new modules: `muse-tools-helpers.ts` (27 LOC) holds the shared `readOptionalString` / `readRequiredDate` / `readOptionalNumber` parsers used across multiple tool builders; `muse-tools-time.ts` (357 LOC) holds the 6 time-domain builders (`createTimeNowTool`, `createTimeDiffTool`, `createTimeAddTool`, `createTimeRelativeTool`, `createNextWeekdayTool`, `createCronForDatetimeTool`) plus their private humanizers (`humanizeRelativeMs`, `humanizeDurationMs`) and the WEEKDAY_NAMES + CRON_DATETIME_MODES tables — all co-located with the only call sites. `muse-tools.ts` now imports the 6 time builders + uses them in the existing `createMuseTools` factory composition; the public surface (`createMuseTools` returning all 17 tools in the same order) is byte-identical, no consumer changes required (verified by smoke:live's `time_now`-using plan-execute test still passing). Round 173's lint sweep + round 174's `no-unused-vars: error` immediately caught a regression mid-edit — the temporary import re-export of `readOptionalString` + `readRequiredDate` was unused after the time tools left, lint refused to pass until pruned. Net total ~+38 lines (overhead from new module headers / import boilerplate) but the main file dropped below 1000 LOC and the time-domain code is now its own unit. Personal-JARVIS dogfood verified: same `time_now` tool still answers `/api/chat` plan-execute live runs through real Gemini. **Caveat / next iter**: the same pattern can be applied to text/markdown/json/data/encoding domains — `muse-tools.ts` still has 11 builders plus `flattenIntoKv` / `deriveMarkdownTableColumns` / `formatMarkdownTableCell` / `parseCsvRecords` / `padBase64` / `slugify` / `evaluateArithmetic` helpers, ~847 LOC. Future iters can pick another domain when the next big-file reduction is needed. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 47/47; `pnpm smoke:live` 12/12; `pnpm lint` 0/0.

- fix (round 178) — third dogfood-discovered bug: `/api/chat` returned 503 `AGENT_RUNTIME_UNAVAILABLE` even when `GEMINI_API_KEY` was exported. The runtime was gated on `MUSE_MODEL` / `MUSE_DEFAULT_MODEL` being explicitly set, but a personal user who exports just `GEMINI_API_KEY` (or `OPENAI_API_KEY` / `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` / `OPENROUTER_API_KEY`) and runs `node apps/api/dist/index.js` should get a working chat endpoint with no further configuration. New exported helper `resolveDefaultModel(env)` in `packages/autoconfigure/src/index.ts` honors `MUSE_MODEL` when set, otherwise infers from credentials in priority order: `GEMINI_API_KEY` / `GOOGLE_API_KEY` → `gemini/gemini-2.0-flash`; `OPENAI_API_KEY` → `openai/gpt-4o-mini`; `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY` → `anthropic/claude-haiku-4-5-20251001`; `OPENROUTER_API_KEY` → `openrouter/google/gemini-2.0-flash-001`. Used in BOTH `createMuseRuntimeAssembly` (for `defaultModel` resolution) and `createModelProvider` (for the provider gate) — they were duplicating `parseOptionalString(env.MUSE_MODEL ?? env.MUSE_DEFAULT_MODEL)` so the fix had to land in both spots, now both go through one helper. Companion private helper `inferDefaultModelFromCredentials(env)` is the inference table; explicit when no key is present returns undefined and the runtime stays disabled (the existing behavior for unconfigured deployments). Added boot-time warning in `apps/api/src/index.ts`: when `options.agentRuntime` is undefined, emit `console.warn` with the exact env vars that need to be set so the user gets actionable guidance instead of a silent 503. 5 new vitest cases in autoconfigure (43 → 48): explicit MUSE_MODEL honored; each of the 4 credential-based inferences (Gemini/Google → Gemini default, OpenAI, Anthropic, OpenRouter); empty env returns undefined; Gemini wins when both Gemini + OpenAI keys present; full `createMuseRuntimeAssembly({ env: { GEMINI_API_KEY: "..." } })` produces a non-undefined `agentRuntime` + `defaultModel: "gemini/gemini-2.0-flash"`. Live dogfood verified end-to-end: `node apps/api/dist/index.js` with only `GEMINI_API_KEY` set now returns `{"content":"ok","model":"gemini-2.0-flash","success":true}` from `/api/chat` (round 176/177 returned 503). Also verified the warning fires when no API key is in env. **Caveat / next iter**: round 177 left an empty-roots regression unfixed — the filesystem MCP server now logs `No valid root directories provided by client` because we advertise the capability but return `[]`. That's the next-priority dogfood bug. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 47/47; `pnpm smoke:live` 12/12; `pnpm lint` 0/0.

- feat (round 177) — closes the second dogfood-discovered gap from round 176: Muse's MCP client now advertises the `roots` capability and serves a `roots/list` handler. Round 176's live boot log surfaced `Client does not support MCP Roots, using allowed directories set from server args` from `@modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem`. The fix is in `packages/mcp/src/transport.ts`: the `Client` constructor receives a second arg `{ capabilities: { roots: { listChanged: false } } }`, and the connector calls `client.setRequestHandler(ListRootsRequestSchema, ...)` returning the configured paths as `file://` URIs (one entry per path, with the absolute path also surfaced as `name` for human readability). New `DefaultMcpTransportConnectorOptions.clientRoots?: readonly string[]` field; autoconfigure wires `parseCsv(env.MUSE_MCP_CLIENT_ROOTS)` so users opt in via comma-separated absolute paths. Default is empty — the capability is still advertised so spec-compliant servers don't log the warning, but no directories are exposed unless explicitly listed (personal-JARVIS conservative default; future per-server-config knobs in mcp.json can override). New `import { pathToFileURL } from "node:url"` and `ListRootsRequestSchema` import from `@modelcontextprotocol/sdk/types.js`. 2 new vitest cases via real-stdio MCP fixture (mcp 116 → 118): roots capability + handler returns the configured paths through SDK round-trip (server-side `server.listRoots()` call returns the matching JSON shape with `uri: "file:///tmp/..."` + `name`); empty `clientRoots` returns `[]` (capability still advertised, no paths exposed). Live verified end-to-end: booting the API server with the same `~/.muse/mcp.json` from round 176 no longer prints the `Client does not support MCP Roots` warning. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 47/47; `pnpm smoke:live` 12/12; `pnpm lint` 0/0. **Caveat**: per-server roots overrides (a Notion server could want different roots than a filesystem server) deferred — the global `MUSE_MCP_CLIENT_ROOTS` is the simplest first knob; per-entry config is a future iter when a real use case appears.

- fix (round 176) — first true dogfood pass surfaces a real bug: `GET /api/health` returned 404 while `GET /health` worked. All other personal-JARVIS routes (`/api/chat`, `/api/notes`, `/api/today`, `/api/tasks`, `/api/voice/*`, etc.) sit under the `/api/` prefix, so users naturally try `/api/health` first — the 404 was a discoverability bug, not a security one. Two-line fix in `apps/api/src/server-routes.ts`: extract a `healthPayload` const, register both `server.get("/health", ...)` and `server.get("/api/health", ...)` returning the same `{ service: "muse-api", status: "ok" }` object. New regression assertion in `scripts/smoke-broad-http.mjs` (broad smoke 46 → 47): "GET /api/health (alias under /api prefix)". The bug was found by the dogfood loop the user explicitly asked about: `pnpm smoke:live` 12/12 first (confirmed CE 1.d / CE 1.e / Notion tasks all survive a real Gemini round-trip — all unverified before this iter), then `node apps/api/dist/index.js` boot + `curl /api/health`. The boot ALSO confirmed round 171's external-MCP seeding works end-to-end against a real `~/.muse/mcp.json` with an `npx -y @modelcontextprotocol/server-filesystem` entry — the autoconfigure log showed `[muse] seeded 1 external MCP server(s)` and the upstream MCP filesystem server actually started on stdio. **Caveats / next iter scope**: (a) MCP filesystem server emitted `Client does not support MCP Roots, using allowed directories set from server args` — Muse's MCP client doesn't advertise `roots` capability, which limits what some upstream MCP servers can do. Future iter. (b) Server boot takes ~3-4s — acceptable for personal use, but not investigated. (c) Dogfood discipline: the user is right that automated tests + diagnostic smoke alone aren't sufficient — at least one `smoke:live` + one manual boot per request/response-touching iter going forward. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 47/47; `pnpm smoke:live` 12/12; `pnpm lint` 0/0.

- feat (round 175) — JARVIS feature: `muse mcp config-path` + `muse mcp config-show` CLI commands. Round 171's `~/.muse/mcp.json` loader gets the file-based ergonomics surface — users can now inspect their config without starting the API server, which is the typical setup-debug + dogfood case. New subcommands inside the existing `muse mcp` group (intentionally distinct from the API-backed `muse mcp list` which queries the running server's registered store): `config-path` prints the resolved file path (honors `MUSE_MCP_CONFIG` override, defaults to `~/.muse/mcp.json`); `config-show` reads + parses the file and prints one row per entry (`<name>\t<transport>\t<config-summary>` — for stdio shows `command=<cmd> args=<json>`, for streamable/sse shows `url=<url>`); `--json` flag emits machine-readable `{ entries, path }`. Missing file → `(no entries — file is missing or has empty mcpServers)` (no error). Malformed JSON / invalid entry shape → stderr message + exit 1 (commander's `command.error`). Also fixes a doc-comment in `commands-mcp.ts` ("Self-contained" was inaccurate after this iter — now imports from `@muse/autoconfigure` for the parser). 4 new vitest cases (cli 34 → 38): `config-path` honors `MUSE_MCP_CONFIG`; `config-show` reports missing-file message; `config-show` prints a row per entry with stdio + streamable summaries; `config-show --json` emits structured `{ entries, path }`. **Caveat / next iter scope**: `muse mcp config-add` (interactive prompt to add an entry) + `muse mcp config-doctor` (validate without printing) deferred — `config-show` already covers the inspection path; `add` requires Clack/Ink interactive flow which is heavier. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46; `pnpm lint` 0/0.

- chore (round 174) — promote lint to `error`: closes the lint setup arc started in round 172. `prefer-const` and `@typescript-eslint/no-unused-vars` move from `warn` to `error`, so any new dead import or never-reassigned `let` blocks `pnpm lint` exit-0. The last warning (`autoconfigure/src/index.ts:388` `let schedulerService`) is fixed by replacing the `let` with a `const schedulerHandle: { current: DynamicScheduler | undefined } = { current: undefined }` holder object — the closure at the tool-registry reads `schedulerHandle.current` instead of the binding directly, so the forward-reference becomes a property mutation (allowed under `prefer-const`) rather than a binding reassignment. After scheduler is built, `schedulerHandle.current = schedulerService` patches the holder. `.claude/rules/code-style.md` updated to reflect the promotion + the holder-object idiom for future authors hitting the same pattern (any closure that needs a forward-reference into a value built later in the same function reaches for the holder, not `let`). 0 errors / 0 warnings now (was 1). `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46. **Caveat / next iter scope**: rules still at `warn` (`no-empty` / `no-useless-escape` / `no-async-promise-executor` / `no-prototype-builtins`) are smaller cleanup targets — promoted only after the codebase has zero violations of each, same discipline as this round.

- chore (round 173) — lint warning sweep: 78 → 1 (the only remaining warning is the known `prefer-const` false-positive in `packages/autoconfigure/src/index.ts:388` where `let schedulerService` is referenced inside a tool-registry closure defined before its assignment site — `let x; x = y;` is required and `prefer-const` doesn't understand the closure forward-reference). Two categories cleaned: (1) **dead barrel re-export imports** — when a file does `import { X } from "./y"` AND a separate `export { X } from "./y"` later, the import line is dead because the export-from doesn't reference the local binding. - feat (round 171) — JARVIS feature: Claude-Desktop-style external MCP config loader. Unblocks the dogfood loop — users can now register external MCP servers (filesystem / github / etc.) by editing `~/.muse/mcp.json` instead of going through the admin REST surface. New `packages/autoconfigure/src/external-mcp-config.ts` (~210 LOC): `loadExternalMcpConfig(env)` reads `MUSE_MCP_CONFIG` (override) or `~/.muse/mcp.json` (default), returns `readonly McpServerInput[]`. Schema mirrors `claude_desktop_config.json` so users copy-paste their existing entries: `mcpServers: { name: { command, args?, cwd?, env? } | { url, transport?, headers? } }`. Transport inference: `command` present → stdio (any explicit `transport` ignored); `url` present → defaults to `streamable`, `transport: "sse"` overrides; neither → `ConfigurationError`. Disabled entries (`disabled: true`) silently skipped. Missing file → empty list (no throw). Malformed JSON / shape errors → `ConfigurationError` with the path + offending key. Companion async helper `seedExternalMcpServers(store, entries)` inserts new entries via `store.save()` and skips names already in the store (so manually-edited DB rows are never clobbered) — returns the list of newly-inserted names so the boot script can log them. `MuseRuntimeAssembly.mcp.externalServerInputs` exposes the parsed list; `createApiServerOptions` adds a parallel `mcpBootstrap: { externalServerInputs, serverStore }` field carrying the boot-time wiring (separate from the narrow route-facing `mcp` field). `apps/api/src/index.ts` now seeds before `server.listen()` and fires `mcp.manager.connect(name)` for each newly-seeded entry (failures logged, never block boot). New `@muse/shared` workspace dep on `@muse/autoconfigure` (was implicit through @muse/mcp). 15 new vitest cases (autoconfigure 28 → 43): stdio entry shape; streamable URL with default transport; explicit `transport: sse`; `disabled: true` skipped; missing `mcpServers` returns []; missing transport (no command + no url) rejected; bad transport value rejected; malformed JSON rejected; non-string env value rejected; `MUSE_MCP_CONFIG` override path; default `~/.muse/mcp.json` path; missing file returns []; real file read + parse round-trip; seed inserts new + skips existing; empty input list returns []. **Caveat / next iter scope**: CLI doesn't yet have a `muse mcp add/list/test` command surface — users hand-edit the JSON; CLI ergonomics is a follow-up. - feat (round 169) — JARVIS feature: Notion tasks adapter (the missing peer to the Notion **notes** adapter from round 128). New file `packages/mcp/src/tasks-providers-notion.ts` (~330 LOC) — `NotionTasksProvider implements TasksProvider` with the same auth + error-mapping shape as `NotionNotesProvider`: 401/403 → `NOTION_AUTH`, 404 → `NOTION_NOT_FOUND`, 429 → `NOTION_RATE_LIMIT`, others → `HTTP_<status>`. Required ctor options `{ token, databaseId }`; optional `titleProperty` (default `Name`), `statusProperty` (default `Status`), `statusOpenValue` / `statusDoneValue` (default `Open` / `Done`), `endpoint`, `notionVersion`, `fetchImpl`. `add(input)` POSTs `/pages` with `parent.database_id`, sets the title on the configured `titleProperty` and the open status on the configured select property. `list(status)` queries `/databases/{id}/query` with a `select.equals` filter when status is `"open"` or `"done"`, paginating up to 10 pages × 100 = 1_000 rows; returns newest-first as Notion delivers them. `complete(id)` PATCHes `/pages/{id}` to set the status select to the done option; returns `undefined` on 404. `search(query, limit)` calls workspace-wide `/search` and narrows results to those whose `parent.database_id` matches the configured database (so unrelated Notion pages never surface as task hits — the notes adapter doesn't bother because workspace-wide notes search is the intent there). `notes` and `tags` from `TaskInput` are dropped on writes for v1 — same conservative scope as Apple Reminders' `tags` drop in round 153. Re-exported from `tasks-providers.ts` barrel and `@muse/mcp` package barrel. `personal-providers.ts` `tryBuildTasksProvider` learns a new `notion` id (silently skips when `MUSE_NOTION_TASKS_TOKEN` or `MUSE_NOTION_TASKS_DATABASE_ID` is missing — explicit opt-in is half-configured during setup) plus optional knobs `MUSE_NOTION_TASKS_TITLE_PROPERTY` / `..._STATUS_PROPERTY` / `..._STATUS_OPEN` / `..._STATUS_DONE`. 9 new vitest cases against a stub `fetchImpl` (mcp 107 → 116, +9 net new): empty-token + empty-databaseId rejected at construction; describe surfaces the configured database; list passes the right select filter and parses rows; add posts the right `parent.database_id` + open-status body; complete patches the status to Done and returns `completedAt` from `last_edited_time`; complete returns undefined on 404; search filters /search hits to the configured database; 401 → NOTION_AUTH + 429 → NOTION_RATE_LIMIT; custom title + status + open-value props honored. **Caveat**: rich-text body + multi_select tags + `status`-property type (vs `select`-property type) deferred to a future iter — the v1 adapter intentionally targets the most common Notion task setup. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46.

- feat (round 168) — Context Engineering **step 1.d wiring**: round 167's `ContextReferenceStore` is now plumbed into the model-loop tool-output truncation path so the agent gets `ref=<id>` in the marker and can call `muse.context.fetch({ ref })` to expand on demand. `packages/agent-core/src/model-loop.ts`: imports `createHash` from `node:crypto` + `ContextReferenceStore` type from `@muse/memory`. `ModelLoopRunner` interface gets an optional `contextReferenceStore?: ContextReferenceStore` field — undefined preserves the legacy round 161 head+tail+marker behavior byte-for-byte. `capToolOutput` (now exported) takes a 4th optional `refStore` arg; when provided AND `output.length > maxChars`, the helper hashes the original output to a 12-hex-char sha256 prefix id and `refStore.put(...)` stashes it before delegating to `trimToolOutput` with a hint that surfaces `ref=<id>, expand via muse.context.fetch({ ref })` inside the marker. Same content → same id, so repeated truncations of identical tool output dedupe (verified by test). All 4 model-loop call sites updated to pass `runner.contextReferenceStore`. `packages/agent-core/src/index.ts`: `AgentRuntimeOptions.contextReferenceStore?: ContextReferenceStore` (with JSDoc explaining the fallback semantics) → private field on `AgentRuntime` → forwarded into `modelLoopRunner()`. `packages/autoconfigure/src/index.ts`: constructs an `InMemoryContextReferenceStore` per process (caps from `MUSE_CONTEXT_REF_MAX_ENTRIES` default 1_000 + `MUSE_CONTEXT_REF_TTL_MS` default 30 * 60 * 1_000), passes it to `createAgentRuntime`, AND registers `createContextReferenceMcpServer({ store })` in the default loopback set so `muse.context.fetch` / `muse.context.list` are exposed as tools the agent can invoke. - feat (round 167) — Context Engineering **step 1.d foundation**: just-in-time retrieval scaffolding via `ContextReferenceStore` + `muse.context` MCP server. Per the round 157 audit, when tools return more content than the per-tool cap (round 161's `trimToolOutput`), the agent should be able to fetch the full bytes on demand rather than have them dumped into context preemptively. New primitive in `@muse/memory`: `InMemoryContextReferenceStore` (~140 LOC) — opaque-id keyed Map with TTL eviction (default 30 minutes — long enough for multi-step task traversal, short enough that refs don't pin memory across sessions) + bounded entry count (default 1_000, oldest-first eviction when reached). Each `ContextReference` carries `id` (caller-supplied, opaque), `content`, optional `contentType` / `source` (tool name) / `originalLength` (pre-truncation byte count). Companion exported interface `ContextReferenceStore` lets future Kysely / Redis-backed impls slot in. New MCP loopback server `loopback-context.ts` (~95 LOC) exposing `muse.context.fetch({ ref })` (returns `{ found: false }` for unknown / expired refs; otherwise returns full content + metadata) and `muse.context.list()` (enumerates cached ref ids + metadata WITHOUT bodies, so the agent can decide whether the budget for `fetch` is worth it). `muse.context` re-exported from `@muse/mcp` barrel. New `@muse/memory` workspace dep added to `@muse/mcp` package.json. Tests added: memory `+2` (`InMemoryContextReferenceStore` round-trip + TTL expiration + cap eviction + delete idempotency / empty-id rejection + `ttlMs=0` never-expires); mcp `+2` (`muse.context.fetch` happy + missing/empty/expired paths / `muse.context.list` returns metadata without bodies). **Caveat**: this is the **scaffolding only** — `trimToolOutput` (round 161) doesn't yet write to the ref store, and autoconfigure doesn't yet register `muse.context` in the default loopback set. Next iter: wire the model-loop tool-output truncation to push large outputs through the ref store and surface `ref=<id>` in the truncation marker, then register `muse.context` in autoconfigure when the store is provided. After that: step **1.e** sub-agent fan-out. memory 60/60 (was 58, +2 net new); mcp 107/107 (was 105, +2 net new); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46.

- feat (round 166) — Context Engineering 1.c **auto-extract upgrade**: the `createUserMemoryAutoExtractHook` LLM extraction now produces typed `veto` and `goal` slots alongside the legacy `facts` / `preferences` records, persisted via `store.upsertUserModelSlot` (the optional method from rounds 164-165). The `systemPrompt` is extended with two new JSON sections — `vetoes: [{id, value, scope?}]` for explicit "do not / never / avoid" rules ("never suggest eggs", "no meetings on Mondays" with scope `"food"` / `"meetings"`) and `goals: [{id, value}]` for multi-session objectives ("ship Muse 1.0 by Q1") — plus inline rules ("Skip single-turn intentions", "Optional scope is a short tag like food, tooling, meetings"). - feat (round 165) — Context Engineering 1.c **DB persistence**: typed user-model slots now round-trip through `KyselyUserMemoryStore`. Three changes flow as one cascade. (1) `packages/db/src/schema.ts` — `UserMemoryTable` gets a new `user_model: JsonColumn<JsonValue | null>` field. Stored as JSONB so the runtime can evolve the slot taxonomy without further migrations; nullable so rows that pre-date this column have no typed slots (the memory layer treats null as `userModel: undefined`). (2) `packages/db/src/migrations.ts` — `CREATE TABLE user_memories` gets a `user_model JSONB` column. No DEFAULT (so legacy reads see SQL NULL, not `'null'::jsonb` confusion). (3) `packages/memory/src/memory-user-store.ts` — `KyselyUserMemoryStore` implements `upsertUserModelSlot` mirroring the InMemory impl from round 164 (replace-by-id within kind via the shared `applyUserModelSlot` helper from the same file). `upsertFact` and `upsertPreference` now thread the existing `userModel` forward when writing legacy fields, so typed slots survive parallel writes. `createUserMemoryInsert` serializes the `userModel` to JSON-safe shape (Date → ISO string for `updatedAt` and `dueAt`); `mapUserMemoryRow` parses the JSONB back, rehydrates Dates, and returns `userModel: undefined` when the column is null OR when every kind array is empty (zero-cost path preserved). New `serializeUserModel` + `slotToJson` + `parseUserModelJson` + `parseSlotArray` private helpers handle the JSONB round-trip with discriminated-union safety (each slot's `kind` is verified on parse so a malformed row can't sneak a `preference` shape into the `goals` array). New `JsonValue` import from `@muse/shared`. 2 new vitest cases (`memory 53 → 55`): typed slots round-trip through `createUserMemoryInsert` → `mapUserMemoryRow` AND through `JSON.parse(JSON.stringify(...))` (simulates a real Postgres JSONB write+read where Dates come back as ISO strings); `null` user_model column on legacy rows maps to `userModel: undefined`. **Caveat**: this is the **persistence primitive**, not yet wired into the auto-extract hook — `createUserMemoryAutoExtractHook` still writes only legacy facts/preferences. Next iter: upgrade the auto-extract hook to populate typed slots from chat content (the LLM call's structured output). - feat (round 163) — Context Engineering 1.c **wiring**: agent-core's `UserMemorySnapshot` now carries the typed `UserModel` field, and `buildPersonaSnapshot` composes typed slots alongside the legacy `Record<string,string>` facts so the agent gets richer signal without dropping backward compat. The composer returns `undefined` for empty models so the call is a no-op for users with no slots set. To exercise the new path end-to-end, callers would have to construct snapshots manually. Next iter: extend `UserMemoryStore` interface + DB schema (`user_memories` table needs a `user_model_json` JSONB column), so the auto-extract hook + persona snapshot resolution naturally round-trip the slots. After that: step **1.d** just-in-time retrieval discipline. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46.

- feat (round 162) — Context Engineering **step 1.c foundation**: typed user-model slots. The legacy `UserMemory` shape stores everything as free-text `Record<string,string>` facts/preferences — the round 157 audit (Letta memory blocks + Anthropic effective-context-engineering) flagged this as a structure-loss issue: a "bedtime" preference and a "favorite color" preference get the same shape even though the agent should treat them very differently. New `packages/memory/src/user-model-slots.ts` (~210 LOC) introduces a *parallel* typed structure (not a replacement, additive — legacy callers stay byte-identical): 5 typed interfaces (`UserPreferenceSlot`, `UserScheduleSlot`, `UserVetoSlot`, `UserGoalSlot` + the `UserModelSlotBase` they extend); the discriminated union `UserModelSlot`; `UserModel` aggregating the 4 slot arrays; `EMPTY_USER_MODEL` constant for zero-cost defaults. Each slot type has its own optional decorators: `UserPreferenceSlot.category` ("style"/"format"), `UserScheduleSlot.recurrence` ("daily 07:00 KST"), `UserVetoSlot.scope` ("food"/"tooling"), `UserGoalSlot.dueAt` + `progress` (0..1, clamped). All slots share `id` (replace-by-id update semantics, no fuzzy match), `value`, optional `confidence` for auto-extract, `updatedAt`. Companion composer `composeUserModelSnapshot(model, { maxPerKind, maxChars })` produces the persona-snapshot string (mirrors `buildPersonaSnapshot`'s contract — returns undefined for empty, single-line `; `-separated key=value form). Output examples: `pref.style.concise=yes; sched.wakeup=morning routine (daily 07:00 KST); veto.food.no-eggs=do not suggest eggs; goal.muse-v1=ship Muse 1.0 (50%, due 2026-03-31)`. Caps: per-kind default 5, total chars default 1_000; both right-truncate with `[N slots elided]` tail. 8 new vitest cases (memory 42 → 50, +8 net new): empty → undefined; preference category prefix; schedule recurrence parens; veto scope tag; goal progress + dueAt decorators; progress clamped to [0,1]; per-kind cap with elided count; total char cap with right-truncation tail. **Caveat / next iter scope**: this is the **type foundation only** — DB persistence (the `user_memories` table needs a `user_model_json` JSONB column or a parallel table), `UserMemoryStore` interface extension, runtime `UserMemoryProvider` snapshot building (today's `buildPersonaSnapshot` reads only the legacy `Record<string,string>`), auto-extract hook upgrade to populate typed slots, and CLI/Web UI surfaces all land in subsequent iters. The composer + types let downstream code start consuming structured slots once a single store grows them. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46.

- feat (round 161) — Context Engineering **step 1.b**: tool-output context-aware trimming. Per Anthropic's effective-context-engineering audit, tool output is the #1 source of context bloat — a single big result (file read / web fetch / DB query) can blow the window in one call. New primitive in `@muse/memory`: `trimToolOutput(input, { maxChars, headRatio?, hint? })` returns `{ output, truncated, originalLength }`. Strategy: head + tail preservation with explicit `[truncated: N chars elided of M total — <hint>]` marker so the agent can see the truncation rather than guessing why the result looks short. Default `headRatio = 0.7` (most tool outputs put headlines at the top). Pure string transform — no I/O, idempotent (marker is shorter than cap by construction). Wired through agent-core: new `maxToolOutputChars?: number` field on `AgentRuntimeOptions` and `ModelLoopRunner`; `executeModelLoop` (and the streaming variant via the same helper) cap each tool's `executed.result.output` BEFORE it lands in `toolMessages` and BEFORE it's joined into the `renderToolResults` summary. Original `executed.result.output` on the tracked tool result is left intact so traces / metrics see full text. autoconfigure default: 8_000 chars (`MUSE_MAX_TOOL_OUTPUT_CHARS=<n>` to override; 0 disables the cap, 8_000 ≈ 2_000 tokens at the rough 4-chars-per-token approximation — large enough for typical replies, small enough that one big result can't blow the working budget). 6 new vitest cases (memory 36 → 42): pass-through when input fits / head+tail preservation with marker / hint surfaces in marker / asymmetric `headRatio=0.9` allocates more head than tail / no-op when `maxChars <= 0` / pathological tiny budget collapses to marker only. **Caveat**: real-LLM smoke (`smoke:live`) wasn't run since this is a no-key environment, but the primitive is pure string and the wiring is straight forward; rounds 162+ will exercise it through autoconfigure-driven runs. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46. **Next iter**: Context Engineering step **1.c** — typed user-memory slots (replace free-text `Record<string,string>` with structured `UserModel { preferences: TypedSlot[]; schedule: ScheduleSlot[]; vetoes: VetoSlot[]; goals: GoalSlot[] }`).

- feat (round 160) — Context Engineering step 1.a **complete**: agent runtime now resolves the persona snapshot from `UserMemoryProvider` and forwards to the trim layer so compactions preserve user-context end-to-end. Round 159 added the primitive (`personaSnapshot` field + injection logic in `@muse/memory`); this iter wires the runtime side. Two new helpers in `packages/agent-core/src/runtime-helpers.ts`: `buildPersonaSnapshot(memory, maxEntries)` produces a compact `fact.<key>=<value>; pref.<key>=<value>; topics=…` single-line form (different shape from `renderUserMemorySection`'s multi-line block — that's for prompt-time injection; this is for budget-tight compaction summaries); `resolvePersonaSnapshot(input, provider, maxEntries)` does the fetch + render and is fail-open (any error / missing memory / missing userId → undefined). `AgentRuntime.run` now resolves the snapshot once per request after `applyUserMemoryFn` and passes it to `prepareModelRequest(input, model, personaSnapshot)`. `prepareModelRequest` merges it into `ConversationTrimOptions.personaSnapshot` only when set, otherwise the legacy path stays byte-identical. Snapshot caps: `maxEntries` facts + `maxEntries` preferences + up to 3 topics; returns undefined for empty memory so under-budget runs pay zero cost. 7 new vitest cases (`agent-core 246 → 253`): `buildPersonaSnapshot` renders `fact.`/`pref.`/`topics=` segments with maxEntries cap (extras dropped, single-line `; `-separated); empty memory → undefined; `resolvePersonaSnapshot` with no provider → undefined; with no userId → undefined; happy path with provider+userId+memory → rendered string; provider error fail-open → undefined; empty memory through provider → undefined. **Caveat**: the `stream()` runtime path also calls `prepareModelRequest` (line 510 in `index.ts` according to the prior `grep`); this iter touched only the non-streaming `run()` path. Streaming path will get the same wiring in the next iter. After that, step 1.b (tool-output context-aware trimming) starts. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46.

- feat (round 159) — Context Engineering step **1.a tail**: persona / user-model snapshot injection at the compaction boundary. When the trim fires (working_budget OR hard_limit) and a compaction summary is being inserted, an optional pre-resolved `personaSnapshot` string from the caller becomes a `[User context: ...]` line in the summary so the agent doesn't lose what it had learned about the user across the boundary. New `ConversationTrimOptions.personaSnapshot?: string` field; new `COMPACTION_PERSONA_SNAPSHOT_PREFIX = "User context"` exported constant for downstream tooling that wants to detect/strip the block. Three guards land with the field: (1) when no compaction fires (under-budget), no `User context` block is added — the feature pays zero token overhead on cheap/short runs; (2) empty / whitespace-only snapshots are treated as absent so callers can pass `""` for "no snapshot this turn"; (3) stale snapshots from a previous compaction round are stripped from the carried-forward summary before the fresh snapshot is appended (no accumulation across multi-round compaction). The strip uses a single-line `User context: ` prefix match — keeps every other summary line intact (compaction summary header, tools, recent topics, pinned entities). The `insertCompactionSummary` + `buildCompactionSummaryText` helpers gain a `personaSnapshot` parameter forwarded from `trimConversationMessages`. 4 new vitest cases (memory 32 → 36): persona snapshot included when trim fires; under-budget run still has no User context line (zero-cost guarantee); whitespace-only snapshot treated as absent; multi-round compaction strips the stale snapshot before appending the fresh one. Caller responsibilities documented inline: caller resolves the snapshot synchronously (e.g. from UserMemoryStore in agent-core/autoconfigure), keeps it short (a few hundred tokens of structured key=value lines, not a full memory dump), treats it as untrusted (no instructions that could mistake for system prompts). `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46. **Caveat**: this is the primitive only — agent-core/autoconfigure don't yet RESOLVE the snapshot from `UserMemoryStore` and pass it in. Next iter (still step 1.a tail finishing): wire `AgentRuntime.run` to fetch the structured user-memory snapshot and forward to `prepareModelRequest` → `trimConversationMessages.personaSnapshot`. Then step **1.b**: tool-output context-aware trimming (round 157's TODO list).

- feat (round 158) — Context Engineering step **1.a** continued: wired the working-budget compaction trigger from round 157 into the actual agent runtime path so it fires for every chat. Three changes flow as one cascade. (1) `AgentContextWindowReport` (in `packages/agent-core/src/types.ts`) gets a new `triggeredBy: "none" | "working_budget" | "hard_limit"` field — observability can now distinguish proactive from forced compaction in dashboards / smoke / future LLM-cost panels. (2) `AgentRuntime.prepareModelRequest` forwards `trimResult.triggeredBy` into the report so every agent run surfaces it. (3) `packages/autoconfigure/src/index.ts:createAgentRuntime`'s `contextWindow` block now computes `workingBudgetTokens` automatically: `Math.floor(maxContextWindowTokens * DEFAULT_WORKING_BUDGET_RATIO)` (= 40% of nominal, the Anthropic + NoLiMa converged ratio). Power users override via `MUSE_LLM_WORKING_BUDGET_TOKENS=<integer>`; setting it to `0` disables proactive compaction (legacy hard-cap-only behavior, opt-out for users who want max history). The auto-default makes the feature on-by-default for every existing assembly (the whole point — round 157's foundation was inert without this wiring). New `DEFAULT_WORKING_BUDGET_RATIO` import added to autoconfigure. 2 new vitest cases (`autoconfigure 26 → 28`): one verifies that with a small nominal window (200 tokens) and 5 conversation turns the runtime fires the **working_budget** trigger (not hard_limit — proves the soft cap is engaged); the other verifies `MUSE_LLM_WORKING_BUDGET_TOKENS=0` disables the feature (`triggeredBy: "none"`, 0 removed). agent-core 246/246 (no test count change — existing AgentContextWindowReport tests still satisfied since the new field is required-but-typed); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46. **Net effect**: every agent run now compacts proactively at 40% of nominal context — quality-during-long-sessions improvement is now live in production assemblies. Next iter (Context Engineering step **1.a's tail**): persona / structured user-model re-injection at the compaction boundary so the agent doesn't lose user context when summarization fires.

- feat (round 153) — second TasksProvider adapter: `AppleRemindersProvider` via `osascript`, mirroring round 129's `AppleNotesProvider` pattern but for macOS Reminders.app. New `packages/mcp/src/tasks-providers-apple.ts` (~330 LOC) implements all 4 ops (`list` / `add` / `complete` / `search`) by piping `tell application "Reminders" ...` AppleScript into `osascript -` and parsing tab-separated structured output. Permissions failures map to a typed `REMINDERS_PERMISSION` error so a CLI wizard can guide the user to System Settings → Privacy & Security → Automation. `tags` are intentionally dropped from `add` — pre-Sonoma AppleScript surface for tags is unreliable; future iter could add tag support behind an opt-in flag once macOS Sonoma+ is stable. The `notes` field round-trips through Reminders.app's body field. - feat (round 145) — pivot iter from refactor-only into actual JARVIS feature work after 6 consecutive `refactor:` rounds. The user pushed back ("무작정 줄이기만 하고있는건 아니지?") — fair check. The personal-domain trio's notes surface had a long-standing wiring gap: `createNotesRegistryMcpServer` (the registry-aware `muse.notes-multi.*` MCP server) existed since round 128's Notion split, AppleNotes + Notion + LocalDir provider classes existed since rounds 128-130, but **autoconfigure never wired them together** — agent had no MCP-tool path to Apple Notes or Notion regardless of how the user configured their env. - fix (round 126) — perf bug in `apps/api/src/today-routes.ts:readRecentNotes`. The handler stat'd every visible note serially via `for (const entry of entries) { await fs.stat(...) }`, so a notesDir with N files cost N sequential round-trips through libuv's thread pool on every `/api/today` request. Same family as round 121's `muse today` CLI fix (which switched 3 sequential `apiRequest` awaits into `Promise.all`) — once you've spotted the pattern in one place, it's worth scanning for siblings, and this is one. Fix: compute the visible-file list with a sync filter first, then dispatch all `fs.stat` calls via `Promise.all`. Per-stat `try/catch` returning `undefined` keeps the failure-isolation semantic so an unreadable file doesn't collapse the whole listing. Existing test in `apps/api/test/server.today.test.ts` (round 123 round-trip with `diary.md` + `shopping.md`) still passes — the visible-file filter and `mtime`-descending sort are byte-identical, only the I/O dispatch shape changed. Net latency: bounded by `max(stat)` instead of `sum(stat)`. api 60/60; `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46.

New assertion fires `GET /api/today?lookaheadHours=12`, asserts 200, `generatedAt` is a non-empty string, the server echoes `lookaheadHours=12` back, and all three sections (tasks / events / notes) come back as arrays — not `undefined` — because smoke broad already wires `MUSE_NOTES_DIR` + `MUSE_TASKS_FILE` to temp dirs (round 114) and the default local calendar provider is registered. Plus a clamp regression: `lookaheadHours=99999` → server returns `168` (the [1, 168] cap from the route handler). Both checks bundled into one `record(...)` block so smoke broad's count moves +1, not +2. smoke:broad 46/46 (was 45, +1 net new); `pnpm check` all green. Net effect: every route in the personal-domain trio + voice surface + the new today consolidator is now covered by at least one smoke-broad assertion.

- fix (round 121) — performance bug in round 119's `muse today` CLI. The doc comment claimed the command "fans out to three existing read-only endpoints in parallel" but the implementation did three sequential `await` calls — `tasks` round-trip, then `events` round-trip, then `notes` round-trip — triple-counting latency for a command users type every morning. Fix: switched to `Promise.all([...])` with per-promise `.catch(() => undefined)` (kept the per-request fallback so a single endpoint failure can't reject the whole `Promise.all`). Inline comment explains the failure-isolation reasoning. Added a regression test `today fans out to all three endpoints concurrently` that gates each stub-fetch response on a barrier released only when 3 requests are observed in-flight, then asserts `maxInflight === 3` — locks in the parallelism so a future maintainer can't accidentally regress to sequential awaits. cli 32/32 (was 31, +1 net new); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 45/45. Net effect: morning briefing is now bounded by the slowest of {tasks, events, notes} round-trips rather than their sum.

- fix (round 117) — real AppleScript bug in `MacOsCalendarProvider`. Six call sites across `listEvents` (×2), `createEvent` (×2), and `updateEvent` (×2) were passing `Date.toISOString()` (the 24-character `YYYY-MM-DDTHH:mm:ss.sssZ` format) into a `do shell script "date -j -f '%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ' '<iso>' ..."` expression. The format string puts a literal `Z` immediately after `:%S` — so a `2026-05-15T10:00:00.000Z` input fails the `date -j` parse on the `.000` and the whole AppleScript chain errors out. Result: every macOS Calendar.app `listEvents` / `createEvent` / `updateEvent` call against a real Calendar silently failed even when permissions were granted. Same family as rounds 105 / 115 (CI-untested AppleScript paths quietly broken). Fix: introduced a private `isoForOsascript(date)` helper that returns `YYYY-MM-DDTHH:mm:ssZ` (millisecond-stripped, 20 chars). Replaced all 6 call sites. Doc comment on the helper explains the `date -j -f` format gotcha so future maintainers don't reintroduce milliseconds. calendar 10/10 (no test changes — real-osascript path stays CI-untested, same precedent as Apple Notes / MacOsCalendarProvider); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 45/45.

- refactor (round 116) — sixth carve into `packages/mcp/src/loopback.ts` (after rounds 82-85 + 96 lifted notes / calendar / tasks / filesystem / fetch). Lifted `createRegexMcpServer` (3 tools: test / match / replace, ~162 LOC including the small `compile` helper that wraps `new RegExp(pattern, sanitizedFlags)` with length-bounding + try/catch) into a sibling `loopback-regex.ts` (189 LOC). Self-contained on top of `@muse/shared` JSON types + the `LoopbackMcpServer` type imported back from `./loopback.js`. Inlined a small `readString` helper. Used the explicit `import { ... } from "./loopback-regex.js"; export { ... };` two-step pattern matching round 85 (filesystem) and round 96 (fetch) because `createRegexMcpServer` is referenced locally inside `createDefaultLoopbackMcpServers` at line 964. `loopback.ts` 1,257 → 1,100 LOC (-157, -12.5%); cumulative across rounds 82-85 + 96 + 116: 2,367 → 1,100 LOC (-1,267, -53.5%, the file is now 46.5% of its original size). mcp 94/94; `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 45/45. The remaining ambient default loopback factories in `loopback.ts` are time / text-utils / math / json / url / crypto / diff — each is single-tool or two-tool and the file's foundation (interfaces + connection adapter + catalog) is intertwined with those. Future iters can keep peeling them off if motivated, or accept that ~1100 LOC of cohesive ambient loopback machinery is fine.

- fix (round 115) — real AppleScript bug fix in `AppleNotesProvider.save` (round 86) for the new-note-creation path. The previous code constructed the AppleScript template `make new note at default account with properties {name:..., body:...}` when no folder was specified, but Notes.app's object hierarchy is account → folder → notes — `note` is NOT a direct child of `account`. The `at default account` form is invalid AppleScript and would runtime-error any new-note-creation call without a folder. Same family of bug as round 105 (delimiter mismatch) and round 106-107 (missing pagination): silent because no CI runner has Notes.app to exercise the real-osascript path. Fix: when no folder is specified, omit the `at` clause entirely — Notes.app then uses the default folder of the default account. The `folder ${quote(folder)}` form was always correct and is preserved. Inline comment added to flag the gotcha for future maintainers. mcp 94/94 (no test changes — real-osascript path stays CI-untested, same precedent as `MacOsCalendarProvider`); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 45/45. The fix takes effect immediately for any user who calls `AppleNotesProvider.save({ title, body })` without a folder argument (the personal-default path).

- test (round 114) — added smoke-broad coverage for the personal-domain REST trio (`/api/tasks/*` and `/api/notes/*`). Smoke broad previously had no end-to-end exercise of either route — round 104 (tasks split) and round 111 (notes added) were both untested in CI by `pnpm smoke:broad`. Two new assertion blocks: (1) `/api/tasks REST round-trips create → list → complete → delete` posts a task, asserts the id is in `/api/tasks?status=open`, marks done via `POST /api/tasks/:id/complete` (asserts `status=done`), DELETEs (asserts 204), then re-lists with `?status=all` to confirm absence; (2) `/api/notes REST round-trips save → list → search → read → append` saves a note, lists entries to confirm presence, searches for an in-content keyword, reads back the body, appends, re-reads to confirm the appended text is present. Critical environment isolation: smoke broad now spawns the API with `MUSE_NOTES_DIR` and `MUSE_TASKS_FILE` pointing at fresh `mkdtempSync` temp directories — `tasks.json` and the notes root never touch the developer's real `~/.muse/...` store. smoke:broad 45/45 (was 43, +2 net new); `pnpm check` all green. Net effect: the personal-domain REST trio (rounds 103-104 + 111) is now fully smoke-broad-covered alongside the existing MCP-tool coverage in the same script — both surfaces verified end-to-end on every CI run.

- refactor (round 113) — second carve into `apps/api/src/server-helpers.ts` (after round 98's auth-identity split). - feat (round 111) — added `/api/notes/*` REST surface, completing the personal-domain trio's REST coverage (calendar already had routes; tasks had routes; notes was MCP-tool-only). New `apps/api/src/notes-routes.ts` (~135 LOC) registers 5 endpoints behind `requireAuthenticated`: `GET /api/notes/list?subdir=`, `GET /api/notes/read?path=`, `GET /api/notes/search?query=&limit=`, `POST /api/notes/save` body `{path, content, overwrite?}`, `POST /api/notes/append` body `{path, content}`. Crucial DRY decision: the route handlers don't reimplement path-safety / fs logic — they wrap `createNotesMcpServer({ notesDir })` and call its tool `execute` callbacks via a `Map<name, ExecuteFn>` lookup. Result: REST surface is byte-identical to the MCP tool surface, sharing the same allowlist-rooted path resolution, file-size caps, and dotfile filtering. Tool error responses (`{error: "..."}`) get HTTP 400; everything else is 200. Added `notesDir?: string` to `ServerOptions`; autoconfigure already had `resolveNotesDir(env)` for the MCP server, so the wiring was a one-line addition: `notesDir: resolveNotesDir(env)` in `createApiServerOptions`. 4 new vitest cases in a new `apps/api/test/server.notes.test.ts`: full save/read/list/search/append round-trip with line-number assertions, unsafe `..%2Fetc%2Fpasswd` path rejection (400), missing-path-required (400), save-without-overwrite collision (400 + "already exists" message) followed by overwrite=true (200), and route-absence when `notesDir` is undefined (404). Either response shape passes; only 5xx, malformed body, or wrong empty/non-empty arrays would fail. - fix (round 107) — completed the Notion-pagination sweep started in round 106. The two remaining `?page_size=100` calls — `NotionNotesProvider.read` (fetching paragraph blocks for the page body) and the private `replaceBlocks` (deleting existing blocks before a save+overwrite) — also silently truncated at 100 children, which would matter for a personal user with a long Notion page (e.g. a daily journal). Factored both into a private helper `fetchAllBlockChildren(pageId)` that loops `start_cursor` / `has_more` up to `NOTION_BLOCKS_MAX_PAGES = 10` (~1000 blocks). `read()` now uses it for body-text aggregation; `replaceBlocks()` uses it so an overwrite genuinely cleans every existing block before re-appending. New regression test (`NotionNotesProvider.read paginates block children via has_more / next_cursor`) stubs `/v1/pages/long` then a 2-page round-trip on `/v1/blocks/long/children` — first call (no `start_cursor`) returns `has_more: true, next_cursor: "blk-2"` with one paragraph; second call (with `start_cursor=blk-2`) returns `has_more: false, next_cursor: null` with another. Asserts both URLs were visited in the right order, the first omits `start_cursor`, the second contains `start_cursor=blk-2`, and the joined body is `"alpha\nbeta"`. The Notion API surface is now pagination-correct on all three places it matters: `/databases/:id/query` (round 106), `/blocks/:id/children` for read, and the same endpoint for replaceBlocks (this iter). mcp 94/94 (was 93, +1 net new); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42.

- fix (round 106) — real bug fix in `NotionNotesProvider.list` (round 87). The original implementation sent `page_size: 100` to `/v1/databases/{id}/query` but never read `has_more` / `next_cursor` from the response, silently truncating any database with more than 100 pages — exactly the personal-Notion-DB-grows-over-time scenario where this would surface unobserved. Fix: rewrite `list()` as a `for` loop that requests up to `NOTION_LIST_MAX_PAGES = 10` (so ~1000 entries cap, after which a personal user really should be searching, not listing) and threads `start_cursor` from each response's `next_cursor` until either `has_more` is false or we hit the page cap. New regression test in `packages/mcp/test/mcp.test.ts` simulates a 3-page round-trip via mocked fetch — first call has no `start_cursor` and returns `has_more: true, next_cursor: cursor-2` with 2 entries, second call sends `start_cursor: cursor-2` and returns `cursor-3` with 1 entry, third call sends `start_cursor: cursor-3` and returns `has_more: false, next_cursor: null` with 1 entry. Asserts all 4 entries surface in order, all 3 request bodies have the expected cursor / page_size shape, and the first request omits `start_cursor`. Same family of bug as round 105 — CI-untested real-API path quietly broken on edge cases. Other Notion endpoints with the same pattern (`/blocks/{id}/children` for read, replaceBlocks delete loop) still cap at 100 — those are individual-page operations where >100 children is rarer; left as future iter scope. mcp 93/93 (was 92, +1 net new); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42.

- fix (round 105) — real bug fix in `AppleNotesProvider.search` (round 86) — silent delimiter mismatch between the AppleScript template and the JS parser. The AppleScript template wrote `& "\\u0000"` between entries, which AppleScript treats as a literal 6-character string `\x00` (it doesn't recognize `\u` Unicode escapes; only `\n` / `\r` / `\t` / `\\` / `\"`). Meanwhile, `parseSearchOutput` in JS used `.split("\x00")` — a single NUL byte (0x00). The two never matched, so split returned the entire output as one logical entry; subsequent `.split("\t")` then read `[firstNoteId, firstNoteName, firstBody+\x00+secondNoteId+\t+secondName+\t+secondBody+\x00+...]` — only the first hit's id/title surfaced, with everything else mashed into its body field. Real bug, but CI-untested because no runner has Notes.app to exercise the actual osascript path. Fix: introduced `APPLE_NOTES_SEARCH_DELIM = "~~~MUSE_NOTES_SEARCH_END~~~"` — a deliberately-unique ASCII marker safe in both AppleScript and JS string-literal contexts. AppleScript template now uses `& "${APPLE_NOTES_SEARCH_DELIM}"` (concrete ASCII) and `parseSearchOutput` splits on the same constant. Doc comment on the constant explains the rationale and warns to keep both sides in sync. Bug found by reading hexdump of the file (`od -c`) — earlier `Read` rendered `\0` as a space, hiding the actual NUL-byte mismatch from quick scans. mcp 92/92 (no test changes — same precedent as `MacOsCalendarProvider`: real-osascript paths stay CI-untested); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42. The fix takes effect immediately for any user who runs `muse.notes.search` against the Apple Notes provider.

- fix (round 97) — voice env-var alignment. Round 95 wired voice to `MUSE_OPENAI_API_KEY`, but that name matched neither the OpenAI SDK convention (`OPENAI_API_KEY`) nor Muse's own model-provider fallback chain (where the OpenAI / OpenRouter / OpenAI-compat adapters all accept `OPENAI_API_KEY` as a fallback after `MUSE_MODEL_API_KEY`). A personal user who set `OPENAI_API_KEY` once — the OpenAI SDK norm and Muse's chat-model fallback — would get chat working but voice silently 404'd because `buildVoiceRegistry` looked for the non-standard `MUSE_OPENAI_API_KEY` only. Fixed `buildVoiceRegistry` in `packages/autoconfigure/src/index.ts` to resolve in this order: (1) `MUSE_VOICE_OPENAI_API_KEY` (Muse-specific override for separate voice billing), (2) `OPENAI_API_KEY` (standard convention, shared with chat). Dropped the orphaned `MUSE_OPENAI_API_KEY` name with a comment in the docstring noting it was a one-iter mismatch. Updated the existing autoconfigure test to use `OPENAI_API_KEY` (the realistic personal-use case), and added a new test asserting `MUSE_VOICE_OPENAI_API_KEY` overrides `OPENAI_API_KEY` when both are set. autoconfigure 23/23 (was 22, +1 net new); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42. Net effect: setting just `OPENAI_API_KEY` now lights up both chat AND voice — one less env var for personal-use setup.

- feat (round 92) — Phase D of the voice-mode rollout: `/api/voice/*` API endpoints. New `apps/api/src/voice-routes.ts` (~150 LOC) with three routes — `GET /api/voice/providers` (describes registered STT/TTS), `POST /api/voice/stt` (decodes base64 audio + mimeType, routes to `VoiceProviderRegistry.requireStt(providerId ?? primary)`, returns `{text, language?, durationMs?, providerId}`), `POST /api/voice/tts` (JSON body `{text, voice?, format?, providerId?}`, returns binary audio body with `Content-Type` matching `result.mimeType` plus `X-Voice-Provider` / `X-Voice-Format` headers). All three behind `requireAuthenticated`. Added `voice?: VoiceProviderRegistry` to `ServerOptions` and wired registration in `buildServer` next to the calendar+tasks block. `VoiceValidationError` → 400 with code; `VoiceProviderError` → 502 with provider+code; missing-provider → 503; route-absent (no registry) → 404. Added `@muse/voice` to `apps/api/package.json` deps. Browser side (Phase E later) can MediaRecorder → base64 → POST `/api/voice/stt`, play `/api/voice/tts` response through `<audio>`. Streaming TTS deferred to Phase F as planned. 8 new vitest cases in `apps/api/test/server.voice.test.ts` covering: provider describe, STT happy path with multipart shape verification, STT empty-audio 400, STT no-provider 503, TTS happy path with header assertions, TTS empty-text 400, TTS provider failure → 502 with `code: HTTP_401`, route absence when registry is undefined. Voice phases A-D done (design + provider abstractions + API endpoints) — remaining: Phase C (`muse listen` CLI with sox), Phase E (web mic button), Phase F (wake-word + streaming + local Whisper.cpp/Piper).
