- fix (round 90) — real bug fix in `apps/api/src/compat-user-memory-store.ts:canAccessUserMemory`. When auth is disabled (the personal-use default with `requireAuth: false` and no `authService`), the function 403'd every `/api/user-memory/:userId` request because the chain was: `currentAuthIdentity` returns undefined (no auth wired) → `canAccessUserMemory` returned `Boolean(undefined?.userId && ...)` = false → `userForbidden` 403. The user-memory CRUD surface (GET / PUT facts / PUT preferences / DELETE) was effectively unusable for the 1-user personal codebase. Fixed by short-circuiting the check when `options.authService` is undefined: in personal mode, any non-empty / non-`anonymous` userId is allowed. The auth-enabled path is unchanged — caller still must be authenticated AND target their own userId. Added a regression test in `apps/api/test/server.admin.test.ts` (`user-memory routes work without auth (personal-use default)`) that builds the server with `buildServer({ logger: false })` (no auth), PUTs/GETs `/api/user-memory/me/preferences`, asserts 200 + correct shape, and verifies the `anonymous` userId still 403s as a denied-corner-case. Also fixed the misleading `userForbidden` error string from `"관리자 권한이 필요합니다"` (admin permission required — there's no admin role) to `"이 사용자 메모리에 접근할 권한이 없습니다"` (no permission to access this user memory). api 45/45 (was 44, +1 net new); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42. The bug had been silent because no smoke test exercised the user-memory routes in personal mode — only the multi-user admin test in `server.admin.test.ts:475-518` hit them with auth enabled.

- chore (round 89) — personal-pivot rename: `authorizeAdmin` → `requireAuthenticated` across the API surface (apps/api, 16 files, 114 occurrences). The function never actually checked an "admin" role — the implementation is `if (!authEnabled) return true; if (getAuthIdentity(request)) return true; reply.status(401)...` — so the "Admin" suffix was Reactor multi-tenant residue (no role tier exists in this 1-user codebase). Single sed pass across `apps/api/src/{admin-session,admin-platform,admin-analytics,admin-observability,admin}-{compat-,}routes.ts`, `mcp-{compat-,}routes.ts`, `compat-{routes,doctor,agent-spec,mcp-proxy}.ts`, `agent-compat-routes.ts`, `scheduler-routes.ts`, `server{,-helpers,-routes}.ts`. Added a doc comment at the definition site explaining the auth-guard semantics and citing the rename rationale. No behavior change — `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42; api 44/44 (unchanged). Naming now matches what the code does (require auth identity when auth is enabled, allow all when disabled), removing the misleading "admin tier exists" implication.

- feat (round 88) — wired `NotesProviderRegistry` into a real MCP surface. New `createNotesRegistryMcpServer({ registry })` factory in `packages/mcp/src/loopback-notes-registry.ts` (~250 LOC) exposes `muse.notes-multi.{providers,list,read,search,save,append}` — six tools matching the existing `muse.notes.*` filesystem-only server but routed through `NotesProviderRegistry` so the agent can target `local` / `apple` / `notion` via `providerId`. `list` and `search` fan out across every registered provider when `providerId` is omitted (per-provider failures swallowed so one bad backend doesn't poison the whole search). `read` / `save` / `append` require `providerId` because their semantics are per-provider. Errors propagate as `{ code, error }` JSON objects (NotesProviderError + NotesValidationError have `code`; generic errors get just `error`). New name `muse.notes-multi` deliberately doesn't collide with the existing `muse.notes` (filesystem-only) server, so both can coexist during the transition; future iter can either deprecate the legacy one or have autoconfigure switch wiring once more than one provider is configured. **Crucially NOT auto-wired into autoconfigure this iter** — that would change the request/response path and require `smoke:live` validation; left for a follow-up. Re-exported `createNotesRegistryMcpServer` + `NotesRegistryMcpServerOptions` through the `@muse/mcp` barrel (`packages/mcp/src/index.ts`). 7 new vitest cases cover: tool-name surface, `providers` describe wrap, `read` round-trip via LocalDir, `search` fan-out across all providers, `save`→`append` round-trip, registry-error propagation (`PROVIDER_NOT_FOUND` for unknown providerId), input-validation rejection without provider invocation. mcp 92/92 (was 85, +7 net new); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42. With this, the priority-4 JARVIS notes triad is complete: LocalDir (real, fully tested) + Apple Notes (real osascript adapter from round 86) + Notion (real api.notion.com adapter from round 87) all reachable through one MCP surface.

- feat (round 87) — replaced the `NotionNotesProvider` NOT_IMPLEMENTED scaffold in `packages/mcp/src/notes-providers.ts` with a real Notion API adapter (~280 LOC). Talks to `https://api.notion.com/v1` with the `Notion-Version: 2022-06-28` header and the integration token. All 5 `NotesProvider` operations: `list()` queries `/v1/databases/{databaseId}/query` (requires `databaseId`, throws `MISSING_DATABASE_ID` otherwise), `read(id)` fetches `/v1/pages/{id}` for metadata + `/v1/blocks/{id}/children?page_size=100` for body and joins paragraph blocks with `\n` (returns `undefined` on 404), `search(query, limit)` posts `/v1/search` with the `object: page` filter, `save({title, body, folder?, id?, overwrite?})` either PATCHes `/v1/pages/{id}` (with optional block replacement when `overwrite: true`) or POSTs `/v1/pages` with `parent.database_id` for new pages, `append({id, body})` PATCHes `/v1/blocks/{id}/children`. Body model is plain text in/out — paragraph per `\n` line — rich-text formatting deliberately not preserved (personal-JARVIS simplification). Status mapping: 401/403 → `NOTION_AUTH`, 404 → `NOTION_NOT_FOUND`, 429 → `NOTION_RATE_LIMIT`, others → `HTTP_<status>`. Constructor injects `fetchImpl` (default: global `fetch`), `endpoint`, `notionVersion`, and `titleProperty` (default `Name`) for testability and customization. Added `NotionNotesProviderOptions` 4 new fields (`titleProperty`, `endpoint`, `notionVersion`, `fetchImpl`). Added 6 unit tests with mocked fetch covering: empty-token rejection, `MISSING_DATABASE_ID`, list-result parsing with auth headers, read 404 + paragraph-join, 401 → NOTION_AUTH, search payload shape. mcp 85/85 (was 79, +6 net new); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42. Both Apple Notes (round 86) and Notion (round 87) adapters now ship real implementations — the only remaining wiring step is to refactor `createNotesMcpServer` to consume `NotesProviderRegistry` so the agent can route between LocalDir / Apple / Notion via `providerId`.

- feat (round 86) — replaced the AppleNotesProvider NOT_IMPLEMENTED scaffold in `packages/mcp/src/notes-providers.ts` with a real macOS-native adapter that shells out to `osascript` against `Notes.app`. Implements all 5 `NotesProvider` operations: `list(folder?)` (every note or `every note of folder "X"`, returns `id\\ttitle\\tfolder\\tisoModDate` lines), `read(id)` (header line `title\\tfolder\\tisoMod` + `\\n` + body HTML), `search(query, limit)` (case-insensitive substring match across body + name with snippet extraction), `save({title, body, folder?, id?, overwrite?})` (creates new note, or updates an existing note's title and optionally body), and `append({id, body})` (concatenates to existing body). Mirrors the proven `MacOsCalendarProvider` shape exactly: `osascriptPath` constructor option (defaults `/usr/bin/osascript`, override in tests), private `runScript` method that pipes script via stdin, typed `NOTES_PERMISSION` / `NOTE_NOT_FOUND` / `EXIT_<code>` error mapping, AppleScript string `quote()` helper that escapes `\\`, `"`, and newlines. Added `AppleNotesProviderOptions { folder?, osascriptPath? }` exported through the `@muse/mcp` barrel. `describe()` now reports `local: true` (was `local: false` for the placeholder) reflecting that the adapter runs against the local Notes.app instance, no network. Replaced the brittle "rejects with NOT_IMPLEMENTED" test with three focused new ones: describe-shape verification, input-validation (`EMPTY_ID` / `EMPTY_QUERY` / `EMPTY_TITLE` before any spawn), and a real osascript-failure smoke that points the adapter at `/usr/bin/false` and asserts the resulting `NotesProviderError` has `code: EXIT_<n>` and `providerId: "apple"`. Real osascript-against-Notes.app paths remain untested in CI (no Notes.app on the runner) — same precedent as `MacOsCalendarProvider`. Not yet wired into autoconfigure or `createNotesMcpServer` — that's a future iter (the design always was: `LocalDirNotesProvider` ships, scaffolds slot in, MCP wiring follows). mcp 79/79 (was 77, +2 net new); `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42.

- feat (round 78) — landed Phase B of the voice-mode rollout: created `@muse/voice` package (`packages/voice/`, ~430 LOC src + 175 LOC tests). Provider-neutral `SpeechToTextProvider` / `TextToSpeechProvider` interfaces with `SttProviderInfo` / `TtsProviderInfo` capability descriptors mirroring `ModelProvider` shape. Default cloud adapters: `OpenAIWhisperSttProvider` (POST `multipart/form-data` to `/v1/audio/transcriptions`, parses `text` / `language` / `duration` from JSON, wraps non-2xx as `VoiceProviderError` with `HTTP_<code>`) and `OpenAITtsProvider` (POST JSON to `/v1/audio/speech`, returns binary audio bytes + format-aware mimeType, supports mp3/wav/opus/aac/flac, voice/format/speed configurable per call). `VoiceProviderRegistry` for STT/TTS lookup. `VoiceValidationError` / `VoiceProviderError` typed error classes. `fetchImpl` injection point on every adapter for unit testing — 16 vitest cases cover happy path + auth error + bad-shape + unsupported format + empty body. No CLI / API / Web wiring yet — Phase C will add `muse listen` next iteration. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42.

- design (round 77) — wrote `docs/design/voice-mode.md` (~140 LOC), the first design doc for the voice JARVIS feature. Three flows scoped (push-to-talk CLI, web mic button, wake-word ambient — last deferred); STT options compared (OpenAI Whisper API as default, Whisper.cpp / Web Speech / Gemini Live / Apple Speech as opt-in); TTS options compared (OpenAI tts-1 default, ElevenLabs / `say` / Piper / Gemini Live as opt-in); mic capture hazards documented (sox dependency for CLI, MediaRecorder for web). Provider-neutral interfaces sketched (`SpeechToTextProvider` / `TextToSpeechProvider`) mirroring the existing `ModelProvider` / `CalendarProvider` / `NotesProvider` patterns. 6-phase rollout plan: A (this doc) → B (`@muse/voice` package skeleton) → C (CLI `muse listen`) → D (API endpoints) → E (web mic button) → F (wake-word + local-only providers). No runtime impact this iter; subsequent iterations can pick Phase B without re-litigating the design space.

- personal-pivot strip (round 76) — dropped the last Reactor-compat Slack/Teams field renames in `apps/api/src/scheduler-routes.ts` (`/api/scheduler/jobs/:id` response). No live consumers (verified via repo-wide grep — no test, smoke, or web-UI reference). **Stability fix**: tightened the smoke:live `muse.notes.search` prompt — was suffering from intermittent Gemini "I need the path first, can you run the search and tell me?" deflection. New prompt explicitly numbers the steps ("Step 1: call muse.notes.search …", "Step 2: take the path … and call muse.notes.read", "Both tool calls are mandatory") and forbids questions/clarifications. - personal-pivot strip (round 75) — dropped Slack residue from cache + tools surface. - feature (round 64) — `createUserMemoryAutoExtractHook` (`packages/memory/src/memory-auto-extract.ts`, ~225 LOC). afterComplete agent hook that runs a small structured-output LLM call against `(latest user prompt, assistant reply)` and persists newly stated facts / preferences into `UserMemoryStore`. Disabled by default (extra LLM call per turn). Enable via `MUSE_USER_MEMORY_AUTO_EXTRACT=true`; override the extraction model with `MUSE_USER_MEMORY_AUTO_EXTRACT_MODEL`. Fail-open at every step (missing userId, malformed JSON, store write fail). Strict system prompt: snake_case keys ≤ 32 chars, values ≤ 200 chars, max 5 facts + 5 preferences per turn. Output sanitiser strips code fences, normalises keys, drops empty values. Avoided agent-core circular dep by duck-typing HookStage / AgentRunContext locally. Tests +4 (happy path, no-userId no-op, malformed JSON fail-open, snake_case + length clamp). `packages/memory test` 28/28.

- feature (round 59) — `/api/calendar/{providers,events,credentials/*}` REST endpoints (`apps/api/src/server-routes.ts` `registerCalendarRoutes`). 5 endpoints: GET `/providers` (registry describe + active ids), GET `/events?fromIso&toIso&providerId` (fan-out or per-provider read), GET `/credentials` (list provider ids with stored credentials), PUT `/credentials/:providerId` (write JSON body to FileCalendarCredentialStore), DELETE `/credentials/:providerId`. - feature (round 58) — `muse setup calendar` interactive CLI wizard (`apps/cli/src/setup-calendar.ts`, ~280 LOC). Multi-select prompts the user for which providers to enable, then walks each: Local confirms storage path; **Google** spins up an ephemeral localhost OAuth callback server (random port, state validation), prints the auth URL, awaits the callback, exchanges the code for a refresh token via the Google token endpoint, persists `{clientId, clientSecret, refreshToken, calendarId}`; **CalDAV** prompts for URL/username/app-password (with iCloud + Fastmail issuance URLs in the help text); **macOS** stores the optional calendar name. Credentials persisted to `~/.muse/credentials.json` (chmod 600 via `FileCalendarCredentialStore`). Wired into `apps/cli/src/program.ts` under a new `setup` command group. `apps/cli/package.json` adds `@muse/calendar`. CLI help surfaces verified — actual OAuth round-trip requires user-issued Google Cloud OAuth client (not exercised in this iter). `pnpm check` all green.

- feature (round 56) — `@muse/calendar` package: provider-neutral calendar abstraction with 4 adapters (Local file, Google Calendar v3, CalDAV, macOS Calendar.app via AppleScript), a `CalendarProviderRegistry` for fan-out, and a chmod-600 `FileCalendarCredentialStore` for persisting OAuth tokens / app-passwords. `LocalCalendarProvider` (full coverage: 20 unit tests for create/list/update/delete + corrupt-file fallback + range filtering + validation) is the only provider verified end-to-end this iter; `GoogleCalendarProvider` / `CalDAVCalendarProvider` / `MacOsCalendarProvider` compile + are unit-test ready but require user-issued credentials / OS permissions to verify against live services. The CLI setup wizard (round 58) and Web UI (round 60) cover the credential entry flow. Architecture mirrors `ModelProvider` so new calendar backends slot in as adapters without touching the agent.

- code quality (round 51) — split guard / response-filter / output-guard pipelines out of `packages/agent-core/src/index.ts`. `index.ts` 1,048 → 914 LOC (-134, -12.8% on top of round 50). Cumulative since round 46: 1,723 → 914 (-47.0%, -809 LOC). New `guard-pipeline.ts` (185 LOC) owns the three guard/filter pipelines around the model call: **`evaluateGuards`** (pre-execution input guards — fails closed, throws `GuardBlockedError` on guard exception or `allowed: false` decision, records guard rejection metric + GuardBlockRateMonitor entry), **`applyResponseFilters`** (post-execution transforms over the model response — fails open, filter exception logged on span without changing the response), **`applyOutputGuards`** (post-execution content guards with allow / modify / reject semantics — fails closed, records output-guard action metric). Each is a free function taking the relevant deps directly: guards/filters/outputGuards arrays, `tracer`, `metrics`, optional `GuardBlockRateMonitor`. AgentRuntime call sites in `run` / `stream` now visibly thread `this.guards` / `this.tracer` / `this.metrics` / `this.guardBlockRateMonitor` etc. — no more hidden `this.*` walks. Pruned orphan imports: `GuardBlockedError` / `OutputGuardBlockedError` direct imports (still re-exported from the errors barrel — line 251), `GuardDecision` / `OutputGuardDecision` type-only imports (kept the re-exports), `ResponseFilterEvidence` (`./runtime-internals.js`). `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42 PASS.

- personal-pivot strip (round 50) — dropped 11 dead `CompatibilityTable` schema stubs from `packages/db/src/schema.ts` + their CREATE TABLE blocks from `packages/db/src/migrations.ts` (-219 net SQL lines / 4 files). They were schema-only ghosts taking up space in the typed `MuseDatabase` and migration script. Net effect: schema now matches code reality — every `MuseDatabase` key has a runtime consumer. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 10/10 PASS.

- code quality (round 49) — split `apps/api/src/server.ts` 1,586 → 658 LOC (-928, -58.5%). - code quality (round 48) — split model invocation loop out of `packages/agent-core/src/index.ts`. `index.ts` 1,280 → 1,048 LOC (-232 LOC, -18.1% on top of round 47). New `model-loop.ts` (298 LOC) owns the react-style model→tool→model orchestration: `executeModelLoop` (blocking, used by `AgentRuntime.run`), `executeStreamingModelLoop` (streaming, used by `AgentRuntime.stream`), and `streamModelTurn` (single-turn provider stream pump that buffers text deltas, captures tool calls, and records token-usage span attributes when the provider emits a usage event). All three are free functions taking a `ModelLoopRunner` facade interface that exposes the 6 needed dependencies (`maxToolCalls`, `tracer`, `metrics`, optional `tokenUsageSink`, `generateWithTracing` callable, `executeToolCall` callable). The previous `planExecuteRunner` adapter unified into `modelLoopRunner` since `ModelLoopRunner` is a structural superset of `PlanExecuteRunner` — single 6-line factory now serves both plan-execute and react-style entry points. `ModelLoopStreamEvent` exported as a typed union (`text-delta` / `tool-call` / `tool-result` / `error` shapes) compatible with the existing `AgentRuntimeStreamEvent` superset. **Pruned orphan imports** from index.ts: `renderToolResults` (`@muse/prompts`), `recordTokenUsageEvent` (`./model-invocation.js`), `recordUsageSpanAttributes` (`./runtime-helpers.js`), `StreamExecutionOptions` / `StreamedModelTurn` (`./runtime-internals.js`). Three modules (plan-execute-loop / context-transforms / model-loop) now own ~870 LOC of formerly-monolithic control flow with explicit dependency edges. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 10/10 PASS (full chat + plan_execute + tool-loop + multi-agent live coverage).

The iter-45 fs-based notes assertions stay. KEEP: `muse.notes` MCP server (filesystem-backed, lands in iter 45 — STAYS). 1원리: a personal user's notes belong in their filesystem; an explicit `muse.notes.search` tool replaces vector retrieval; the runtime no longer carries dead RAG infra it can't justify. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 42/42 PASS (was 48 — 6 dropped as listed); `pnpm smoke:live` 10/10 PASS.

- personal-pivot feature swap — `muse.notes` MCP server: RAG-retriever-backed → filesystem markdown-backed (+354 net lines / 6 files). The previous iter wired `muse.notes.search` to the implicit RAG retriever (BM25 over RagDocumentStore). Design rethink: a personal user's notes belong in *their* filesystem (Obsidian vault, git-tracked markdown, plain `~/.muse/notes`) — not in Muse's PG-backed RAG cache. Filesystem ownership > vector embedding for personal use. Replaced the single `search` tool with five filesystem-sandboxed tools: `muse.notes.list({ subdir? })` (non-recursive directory entries with size + isDirectory), `muse.notes.read({ path })` (UTF-8, capped at maxFileBytes=1MB default), `muse.notes.search({ query, limit? })` (case-insensitive substring grep across `.md`/`.markdown`/`.txt` files, returns `{ matches: [{ path, line, snippet }] }`), `muse.notes.save({ path, content, overwrite? })` (creates parent directories, errors on dup unless overwrite), `muse.notes.append({ path, content })` (tail-append for daily journals). All paths resolved relative to a single `notesDir` root with strict path-traversal guards (`..`, absolute paths, sandbox-escape resolves all error). Autoconfigure: `MUSE_NOTES_DIR` env (default `~/.muse/notes`, auto-`mkdirSync({ recursive: true })`), `MUSE_NOTES_ENABLED=false` to disable. Replaces the previous ragPipeline-gate; notes server now registers regardless of RAG state. Tests: 6 unit cases covering save/read round-trip, overwrite semantics, append, list, search line-numbers, path-traversal rejection, 5-tool registration shape with correct read/write risk levels. smoke:broad (48/48): replaced 2 RAG-based assertions with 2 fs-based ones (full save→search→read round-trip in tmpdir; absent when `MUSE_NOTES_ENABLED=false`). smoke:live (10/10): seeds two markdown files in tmpdir before spawning the API with `MUSE_NOTES_DIR` set, prompts Gemini to "use muse.notes.search to find what to buy for mom's birthday", asserts `toolsUsed` includes `muse.notes.search` and the answer surfaces note content (`white`/`jeju`). Cleanup `rmSync` on exit. 1원리: personal notes live in the user's filesystem (Obsidian/iCloud/git/wherever); Muse should *touch* them, not own them. Vector RAG infra is separate concern (next iter likely strips the now-unused `packages/rag` retriever wiring + implicit-RAG context injection). `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 48/48 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 10/10 PASS.

- personal-pivot default flip — `MUSE_RAG_PIPELINE_ENABLED` default flipped `false → true` (+15 / -7 / 4 files). For a personal user, RAG over personal notes is the JARVIS-defining capability — it should not be off-by-default. Reactor's "off-by-default to preserve current no-RAG behavior" stance was a SaaS-migration guard; for the personal pivot the right default is on. Implementation: `parseBooleanFlag` in `packages/autoconfigure/src/rag-query.ts` now takes a `fallback = false` arg and recognizes the explicit `false`/`0`/`no` strings so `MUSE_RAG_PIPELINE_ENABLED=false` still works to disable; `createDefaultRagPipeline` calls it with `fallback=true`. Smoke broad case `notes.search registers when ragPipeline is enabled` rewritten to assert default-on (no env hint), the `absent when ragPipeline disabled` case now uses `MUSE_RAG_PIPELINE_ENABLED: "false"` explicitly. `rag-query.test.ts` updated: rewrote `returns undefined unless MUSE_RAG_PIPELINE_ENABLED=true` as `returns undefined when MUSE_RAG_PIPELINE_ENABLED=false explicitly disables RAG` plus a new `defaults to enabled when unset` test. The previously-required `MUSE_RAG_PIPELINE_ENABLED: "true"` in smoke:live env is now redundant — left in place for documentation. 1원리: a personal JARVIS without RAG over personal notes isn't a JARVIS, it's a chat client. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 48/48 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 10/10 PASS.

- JARVIS-style feature — added `muse.notes.search` loopback MCP tool (+236 net lines / 6 files). The agent can now explicitly look things up in the user's RAG-indexed personal notes via `muse.notes.search(query, limit?=5, max=20)` rather than relying solely on the implicit RAG context injection that fires on every run. Implementation: `createNotesMcpServer({ retriever })` in `packages/mcp/src/loopback.ts` exposes a single `search` tool that accepts a query (≤1000 chars) and an optional limit (clamped 1..20), forwards the query to the configured `DocumentRetriever`, and returns `{ matches: [{ id, content, score, source? }] }`. `NotesDocumentRetriever`/`NotesDocumentMatch` interfaces are duck-compatible with `@muse/rag`'s `DocumentRetriever`/`RetrievedDocument` so we keep the package boundary (mcp doesn't need to import @muse/rag). `packages/autoconfigure` auto-registers the loopback whenever `MUSE_RAG_PIPELINE_ENABLED=true` (matching the implicit-RAG gate) by appending it to the `DynamicToolRegistry` source list and threading `createDocumentStoreRetriever(ragDocumentStore)` into the factory. Tests: 4 unit cases in `packages/mcp/test/mcp.test.ts` (matches passthrough, limit clamping + whitespace trim, empty/overlong-query rejection, `MuseTool` registration shape — `muse.notes.search`, risk=read), 2 smoke-broad cases (registers when ragPipeline enabled + seeded docs return matches; absent when ragPipeline disabled), 1 smoke-live case (Gemini round-trip: seed two notes via `/api/admin/rag/seed-policy`, prompt LLM to `Use the muse.notes.search tool to find...`, assert `toolsUsed` includes `muse.notes.search` and the content surfaces in the answer). 1원리: implicit RAG covers "the agent quietly knows about your notes" but doesn't cover "the agent says 'let me check your notes'" — making it an explicit tool turns it into a JARVIS-shaped affordance. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 48/48 PASS (was 46); `pnpm smoke:live` 10/10 PASS (was 9). The live test confirms end-to-end personal-JARVIS behavior: real LLM, real retriever, real tool call, real note-content quoted back.

- JARVIS tool expansion — added `cron_for_datetime` zero-IO ambient utility (+82 src lines / 4 files). The bridge tool that converts an ISO-8601 datetime to a cron expression for the scheduler so the LLM can compose natural-language reminders deterministically: `time_now` → `time_add`/`next_weekday`/`time_relative` → `cron_for_datetime` → `scheduler_create_job`. Four modes: `once` (default, yearly-recurring at exact minute/hour/day/month — disable the job after fire for true one-shot), `daily` (every day at hour:minute), `weekly` (every week on UTC weekday at hour:minute), `monthly` (every month on day-of-month at hour:minute). Returns `{ cron, iso, mode }`. Bounded errors: missing iso, invalid ISO-8601 format, unknown mode. Tests cover Sunday once-mode, daily, weekly (case-insensitive WEEKLY), monthly, all 3 error paths. Toolset 16 → 17; the `registers sixteen` test header rewritten as `registers seventeen`; smoke:broad required-names list extended. 1원리: a personal JARVIS user wants to say "remind me tomorrow at 3pm to call mom" and have it scheduled — the existing scheduler insists on cron, the existing time tools resolve relative dates, but nothing bridged ISO datetime to cron. `cron_for_datetime` is that bridge. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.

- personal-pivot strip (round 35) — dropped the guard rule editor admin UI surface (-2449 net lines / 21 files). The "admin can edit input/output guard rules at runtime via UI" CRUD layer was Reactor's SaaS governance pattern: an operator opens an admin console, writes regex patterns into rule rows, simulates them against sample inputs, reorders the pipeline stages, and audits each rule edit. For a personal JARVIS user there is no admin separate from the user, no operator-author distinction, and no scenario where editing a JSON rule row in a UI is faster than editing env config. Personal users get safety guards from runtime / env config — `findInjectionPatterns`, `maskPii`, `detectSystemPromptLeakage`, the `topic-drift` heuristic, the `tool-output-sanitizer` filter, the `adversarial-red-team` block all live in `@muse/policy` and run on every `/api/chat` request without any rule-row authoring. imports, the `guardRuleStore?: GuardRuleStore` field on `ReactorCompatibilityRouteOptions`, `inputGuardRules`/`outputGuardRules`/`outputGuardRuleAudits` Maps from `CompatState`, the - personal-pivot strip (round 34) — dropped TokenRevocationStore + auth_token_revocations table (-172 net lines / 8 files). For a personal user, server-side JWT revocation tracking is overkill — the token expires by `exp` claim, and on any JWT-secret rotation all outstanding tokens become invalid anyway. The "logout immediately invalidates this JWT server-side" behavior is a SaaS multi-session concern (operator wants to kick a stolen device). Removed: `TokenRevocationStore` + `AsyncTokenRevocationStore` interfaces; `InMemoryTokenRevocationStore` + `KyselyTokenRevocationStore` classes; `TokenRevocationStoreType` type + the `tokenRevocationStore`/`tokenRevocationStoreStrict` fields on `AuthProperties`; the `revocationStore` field on `AuthOptions`/`AsyncAuthOptions` + the `Auth`/`AsyncAuth` member; the revocation branches in `authenticateBearer`/`logout` (logout now just returns `Boolean(jwt.parseToken(token))` — token expires naturally); `createAuthTokenRevocationInsert` helper + `AuthTokenRevocationInsert` Kysely type + `AuthTokenRevocationTable` import; `auth_token_revocations` CREATE TABLE + index from migrations + the table interface from schema + the entry from migrations.test.ts; the wiring in autoconfigure (drop the `revocationStore: new KyselyTokenRevocationStore(db)` / `new InMemoryTokenRevocationStore()` calls); the `revocations.size()` test assertion; the `logout revokes the token so authenticateBearer returns undefined afterwards` test rewritten as `logout returns true for a parseable token (no server-side revocation)`. 1원리: a personal user with one session at a time has no scenario where server-side JWT revocation matters — close the tab, the token still works until exp, but nobody's stealing it from a 127.0.0.1 binding. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.

- personal-pivot strip (round 33) — dropped `AuthRateLimiter` brute-force protection (-237 lines / 8 files). For a personal user with one local account on a 127.0.0.1 binding there is no abuse surface — the rate limiter existed to defend SaaS login pages from credential-stuffing attacks. Removed: `AuthRateLimiter` class + `AuthRateLimiterOptions` interface from packages/auth (with the now-unused `defaultRateWindowMs` constant); `authRateLimiter` field on `ServerOptions` + `ReactorCompatibilityRouteOptions`; the auto-construct `new AuthRateLimiter()` in `buildServer`; the rate-limit gate from both `/api/auth/login` (compat-routes) and `/auth/login` (server.ts native); the `authRateLimitKey` helper from `compat-auth.ts` + `server.ts` + the re-export; the `AuthRateLimiter` test blocks in `auth.test.ts` (1) + `auth-hardening.test.ts` (3) + `server.test.ts` (1). 1원리: brute-force defenses are a multi-tenant authentication concern — for a personal user, the password is never being typed by an attacker, and even if someone got network access to the binding they could just hit the password file directly. `pnpm check` all green; `pnpm smoke:broad` 46/46 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.

- personal-pivot strip (round 32) — dropped enterprise SSO surface: IamTokenExchange + /api/auth/exchange + /api/auth/demo-login + maskedAdminAccountRef + resolveIamRole (-282 net lines / 7 files). Reactor's IAM-token-exchange flow let an enterprise SSO provider hand a third-party JWT to the auth service, which then verified it and issued a Muse JWT — pure B2B SSO bridging code that has zero meaning for a personal user with one local account. The `/api/auth/demo-login` endpoint registered a fake "Demo Admin" user and force-promoted it to admin role — onboarding theatre for a multi-user demo deployment that doesn't apply when there's exactly one real user. The `maskedAdminAccountRef` helper was a SOC-2-style admin-actor-redaction utility (sha256(actor).slice(0,12) → "admin-account:abc123def456") for compliance audit logs that no longer exist. The `resolveIamRole(roles, default)` helper mapped Spring's ROLE_ADMIN/ROLE_USER taxonomy onto Muse's role field — dead with IAM exchange gone. - personal-pivot strip (round 31) — dropped workspace_id field + the entire channel-keyed tool-policy mechanism (-882 net lines / 25 files). - personal-pivot strip (round 28) — dropped 2 granular cache-invalidation endpoints `/api/admin/platform/cache/{invalidate-key,invalidate-by-pattern}` (-58 net lines / 3 files). Both were SaaS multi-tenant ops surfaces: `invalidate-key` lets an operator drop one specific cache entry by key, `invalidate-by-pattern` lets them drop entries matching a glob pattern (Reactor's "invalidate cache for tenant X" workflow). For a personal user there is no scenario where granular per-key or per-pattern invalidation matters — the only "is the cache stale?" answer is "kill it all and re-run." The kill-all switch survives at `/api/admin/platform/cache/invalidate` (Reactor-compat) and `DELETE /admin/cache` (native). Removed: 2 routes from `admin-platform-compat-routes.ts` (the docstring `cache/{invalidate,invalidate-key,invalidate-by-pattern}` line trimmed to `cache/invalidate`), 2 manifest entries from `compatibilityApiPaths()`, the 4 test injects (`platformCacheInvalidateKeyMissing`, `platformCacheInvalidateKey`, `platformCacheInvalidatePatternMissing`, `platformCacheInvalidatePattern`) and the 6 corresponding expects (status-400 "key is required", `{cacheEnabled:false,invalidated:false}`, status-400 "pattern is required", `{cacheEnabled:false,invalidatedCount:0}`). The cache `invalidate(key)` / `invalidateByPattern(pattern)` methods themselves stay on the `ResponseCache` interface — `admin-routes.ts` still has `DELETE /admin/cache/:key` and `POST /admin/cache/invalidate-pattern` using them; their cleanup is a separate iteration's concern. 1원리: granular cache invalidation is a SaaS operator tool — for personal use the cache is either fresh enough or it's dead, with nothing in between worth the dedicated endpoint. `pnpm check` 1034 passed / 7 skipped (~6 individual assertions removed); `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.

[]`) for when `operations` was undefined — but the non-tenant paths route through `requireOperations(...)` which returns 503 in that case, which is the honest answer (when operations isn't configured, surfacing fake-empty fallbacks pretends the system has cost/alert/SLO data when it doesn't). - JARVIS tool expansion — added `base64` zero-IO ambient utility (+76 src lines / 3 files). Single tool with `mode: "encode" | "decode"`: encode converts UTF-8 `text` to base64; decode converts base64 `text` back to UTF-8 with a strict round-trip validator (`Buffer.from(input).toString("base64").replace(/=+$/, "")` must equal the input minus padding — Node's permissive base64 parser silently drops invalid bytes otherwise, which would let garbage inputs through). Optional `urlSafe: true` flag swaps alphabet to `-`/`_` and drops `=` padding on encode; on decode accepts URL-safe input and re-pads/normalises before parsing. Per-mode regex gate rejects characters outside the alphabet (`/^[A-Za-z0-9+/]*={0,2}$/` standard, `/^[A-Za-z0-9_-]*={0,2}$/` URL-safe). Bounded inputs: text ≤ 500k characters. Tests: standard encode + decode round-trip, URL-safe round-trip on `"??>>"` (which exercises both `+` → `-` substitution and `=` padding drop), UTF-8 multibyte round-trip on `"안녕"` → `"7JWI64WV"`, invalid mode rejected, invalid base64 rejected. Toolset 15 → 16; the `registers fifteen zero-IO ambient utility tools` test header rewritten as `registers sixteen`; smoke:broad required-names list extended. 1원리: inspecting JWT payloads, decoding opaque tokens, and constructing basic-auth headers are all routine personal-JARVIS operations — but asking the model to do base64 inline is wasteful and error-prone, especially with multibyte UTF-8. The deterministic tool offloads it. `pnpm check` 1034 passed / 7 skipped (1 new test); `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.

- JARVIS tool expansion — added `next_weekday` zero-IO ambient utility (+66 src lines / 3 files). Resolves a weekday name (e.g. `"Monday"` / `"mon"` / `"TUES"`, case-insensitive, accepts 3-letter abbreviation aliases for every weekday) to the next ISO date on which it falls. Optional `reference` (ISO-8601) pins the comparison point; otherwise the injected clock is used. Strict-future semantics: when the reference itself falls on the requested weekday, returns the occurrence one week later. Returns `{ iso: "YYYY-MM-DD", weekday: "<canonical name>" }` (UTC date stripped of time-of-day). Internal `WEEKDAY_NAMES` table maps each canonical name + aliases (`sunday`/`sun`, `monday`/`mon`, `tuesday`/`tue`/`tues`, `wednesday`/`wed`, `thursday`/`thu`/`thur`/`thurs`, `friday`/`fri`, `saturday`/`sat`). Tests: Thu reference → next Mon, alias 'mon' resolves the same date, same-weekday reference rolls a full week forward, default-clock fallback (injected fixture clock = 2026-05-07 Thu → next Sun = 2026-05-10), empty input → error, unknown weekday → error listing the seven canonical names. Toolset 14 → 15; the `registers fourteen` test header rewritten as `registers fifteen`; smoke:broad required-names list extended. 1원리: scheduling reminders by weekday ("remind me next Monday") is a JARVIS-personal staple — `next_weekday` resolves the verbal phrase to a concrete ISO date deterministically, with no inline math from the model. `pnpm check` 1032 passed / 7 skipped (1 new test); `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.
- personal-pivot strip (round 17) — collapsed the 3-state alert lifecycle (`open` / `acknowledged` / `resolved`) to 2-state (`open` / `resolved`) (-69 net lines / 4 files). Personal users see an alert once and either dismiss it or it stays open — the intermediate "acknowledged" state existed for SaaS triage workflows where one operator acks while another resolves. Removed: `POST /admin/alerts/:alertId/ack` route, `acknowledgeAlert(id)` method on `AdminOperationsStore` interface + InMemory + Kysely impls, `acknowledgedAt?` field on `AdminAlert`, `acknowledged_at` write-side field in resolveAlert (DB column survives schema-untouched + insert pins to null). `mapAdminAlertRow` defensively coerces legacy `"acknowledged"` rows to `"open"` so old data still parses. `AdminAlertStatus` literal narrows from 3 → 2 values. Tests: server.test.ts loses the ack inject + assertion; runtime-state.test.ts drops `acknowledgeAlert` call + ack assertion (createAlert still runs to satisfy listAlerts length=2 expectation). 1원리: a 3-state lifecycle is an SaaS team-triage construct — personal user wants "I saw it, kill it." `pnpm check` 1031 passed / 7 skipped (1 assertion removed); `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.

- JARVIS tool expansion — added `csv_parse` zero-IO ambient utility (+121 src lines / 3 files). Parses CSV `text` into structured rows: with `header: true` (default) the first record becomes column names and remaining records return as objects keyed by those names plus a `headers` field; with `header: false` every record returns as an array of strings under `rows`. Internal `parseCsvRecords(text)` handles quoted fields (`"…"`), escaped quotes (`""` → `"`), CRLF + LF line endings, and trailing empty fields via a small character-by-character state machine — no regex, no library. Bounded inputs: text ≤ 200k characters, ≤ 1000 records (data rows in header mode). Empty text returns `{ rows: [] }`. Tests cover header parsing with mixed quoted/unquoted fields, escaped quotes inside a multi-line cell, CRLF round-trip, header:false array form, and empty-input. Toolset 13 → 14; the `registers thirteen` test header rewritten as `registers fourteen`; smoke:broad required-names list extended. 1원리: personal users routinely paste CSV from spreadsheets — letting the model parse it inline is brittle (escaped commas, quoted newlines), so `csv_parse` lifts the parsing into deterministic code with bounded cost. `pnpm check` 1033 passed / 7 skipped (1 new test); `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.
- JARVIS tool expansion — added `hash_text` zero-IO ambient utility (+44 src lines / 3 files). Computes a hex digest of `text` using `algorithm` (default `sha256`, also `sha1` and `md5`). Hashes the UTF-8 bytes of the input via Node `crypto.createHash`. Algorithm input is lowercased before lookup so `"MD5"` resolves; unknown algorithms return `{ error: "algorithm must be one of: sha256, sha1, md5 (got '…')" }`. Tests cover sha256/sha1/md5 fixed digests, empty-string sha256, and unknown-algorithm rejection. Toolset 12 → 13; the `registers twelve` test header rewritten as `registers thirteen`; smoke:broad required-names list extended. 1원리: deterministic content fingerprints (note dedup, stable IDs derived from prompts, change detection on attached payloads) are routine personal JARVIS needs — `hash_text` lets the model do them without piping through a string library or a separate tool. `pnpm check` 1032 passed / 7 skipped (1 new test); `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.

- JARVIS tool expansion — added `markdown_table` zero-IO ambient utility (+93 src lines / 3 files). Renders an array of plain JSON objects as a GitHub-flavored markdown table. Columns default to the union of keys from the first 50 rows (first-appearance order); pass `columns` to constrain or reorder. Cell values render via `String()`; `|` characters escape to `\|` and newlines escape to `<br/>`. Empty input returns the empty string. Capped at 200 rows with a trailing `_…N more rows omitted_` line on overflow. Three small helpers: `deriveMarkdownTableColumns`, `formatMarkdownTableCell`, plus the factory itself. Tests cover basic rendering, explicit-column override + reorder, pipe + newline escaping, empty input, 205-row truncation. Toolset 11 → 12; the `registers eleven` header rewritten as `registers twelve`; smoke:broad required-names list extended. 1원리: when the model wants to surface tool output as a tabular answer, asking it to format markdown by hand wastes tokens and is error-prone — `markdown_table` does it deterministically. `pnpm check` 1031 passed / 7 skipped (1 new test); `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.

- JARVIS tool expansion — added `kv_summarize` zero-IO ambient utility (+77 src lines / 3 files). Flattens a JSON object or array into newline-joined `key: value` lines: nested keys joined with `.`, array indices appear as `.0`, `.1`. Strings/numbers/booleans/null render directly; nested arrays + objects recurse. Empty object → `value: {}`, empty array → `items: []` (or `value: []` at root). Capped at 200 lines with a trailing `…(N more)` line when truncated. Recursive flattener `flattenIntoKv(value, prefix, emit)` keeps the implementation small. Tests cover flat object, nested object + array dot-paths, empty object, empty array. Toolset 10 → 11; the `registers ten` header rewritten as `registers eleven`; smoke:broad required-names list extended. 1원리: when a tool returns a structured object the model shouldn't have to parse JSON to fold it into prose — `kv_summarize` is the natural pre-step that makes the result legible without any custom prompt scaffolding. `pnpm check` 1030 passed / 7 skipped (1 new test); `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.
- JARVIS tool expansion — added `regex_extract` zero-IO ambient utility (+71 src lines / 3 files). Given `{ pattern, text, flags? }`, returns `{ matches: string[] }` with up to 1000 entries: when the pattern has no capturing group each item is the full match, when there is at least one group each item is the first captured group. Bounded inputs: text ≤ 100k chars, pattern ≤ 500 chars, flags must be a subset of `g/i/m/s/u/y` (rejects others); the `g` flag is force-included so iteration semantics work; invalid pattern → `{ error: "invalid pattern: …" }`. Tests cover: email-style global match, capturing-group preference (`<(\\w+)>` → first-group strings), invalid flags rejected, malformed pattern surfaced as error, empty pattern → `{ error: "pattern is required" }`. Toolset goes 9 → 10; the "registers nine zero-IO ambient utility tools" header rewritten as "registers ten"; smoke:broad required-names list extended. 1원리: personal JARVIS users routinely ask "pull all dates / emails / phone numbers from this paragraph" — `regex_extract` is more precise than asking the model to do the regex inline, and 1000-cap + size guards keep it bounded. `pnpm check` 1029 passed / 7 skipped (1 new test); `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.

- JARVIS tool expansion — added `url_parts` zero-IO ambient utility (+51 src lines / 3 files). Parses an absolute URL into `{ protocol, host, port, path, query, hash, origin }` — protocol stripped of trailing colon, port returned as `number` when explicit and `null` otherwise, query exposed as a decoded `Record<string, string>` (last-write-wins), hash stripped of leading `#`. Invalid input returns `{ error: ... }`. The factory uses the platform `URL` class for parsing — no regex, no string library, deterministic + read-risk + zero IO. Test coverage: explicit-port + query + hash + path round-trip, no-port → port: null, empty → error, "not-a-url" → error. The `createJarvisTools()` toolset goes from 8 → 9; the test header rewritten "registers eight zero-IO ambient utility tools" → "registers nine"; smoke:broad required-names list extended. 1원리: personal JARVIS routinely classifies links by host, pulls a single query parameter, or composes new URLs — `url_parts` is more direct than asking the model to do string surgery, and faster than any tool round-trip. `pnpm check` 1028 passed / 7 skipped (1 new test); `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.

"default"` (a Slack workspace id misused as a tenant identifier) — the field is removed from the response shape. `packages/eval/src/index.ts` `createDebugReplayCaptureInsert` pins `tenant_id: "default"` instead of reading `record.tenantId` (the DB column survives schema-untouched), and `mapDebugReplayCaptureRow` no longer projects the column back as `tenantId` — `/api/admin/debug/replay` + `/api/admin/debug/replay/{id}` responses lose the field. - JARVIS tool expansion — added two zero-IO ambient utility tools to `createJarvisTools()` (+113 src lines / 3 files): (a) `time_relative` — given an ISO-8601 `at` (and optional `reference`), returns `{ humanized, deltaMs, direction: "past"|"future"|"now" }` with phrases like "in 2h", "3d ago", "just now"; complements the existing `time_now` / `time_diff` / `time_add` triplet for "when" answers. (b) `slugify` — converts free-form `text` to a URL-safe slug (lowercase, alnum-only, runs collapsed to `-`, leading/trailing dashes stripped, optional `maxLength` truncation that re-trims trailing dashes); empty inputs return `"untitled"`. Both are pure deterministic + read-risk + zero IO. Internal helpers `humanizeRelativeMs(ms)` and `slugify(text, maxLength?)` added next to the existing `humanizeDurationMs`. "default"`. `createCostAnomalyHook` (integrations) drops `tenantIdFromContext` option + `tenantId` field of the notify event payload — `recordCost` is called directly when `budgetTracker` is configured. autoconfigure drops `MUSE_BUDGET_MAX_TENANTS` env knob + `budgetTenantIds` wiring. `apps/api/admin/jarvis/snapshot` wire format changes from `budgets[]` → `budget` (single). 1원리: a single personal user has exactly one budget bucket — per-tenant keying, FIFO eviction, and `tenantIds()` enumeration are all noise that adds 50+ lines of bookkeeping to track a Map of size 1. `pnpm check` 1029 passed / 7 skipped (1 maxTenants test removed); `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS (one assertion updated for `budget` singular shape); `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.

Tests reorganized to assert via `not.toHaveProperty("adminScope")` so the absence of the field is verified. 1원리: a single user's metric events carry no per-tenant attribution, and the role itself already encodes the only admin-scope distinction left. `pnpm check` 1029 passed / 7 skipped; `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS.

- live SSE bug fix — `/api/chat/stream` now emits the full plan-execute event sequence in reactor responseMode too. Bug: the `toSseStream` adapter gated `plan-generated` / `plan-step-executing` / `plan-step-result` / `synthesis-started` events behind `responseMode !== "reactor"`, so the reactor-prefixed `/api/chat/stream` endpoint silently dropped all of them — clients only saw the final `event: message` and `event: done`. The diagnostic-provider `smoke:broad` test was on `/chat/stream` (extended mode) so the gate was invisible there; only `smoke:live` (which targets `/api/chat/stream`) caught it. 1원리: a stream client doesn't care which prefix the URL has — plan-execute mode either emits its lifecycle events or it doesn't, the choice should not depend on URL convention. `tool_call` vs `tool_start/tool_end` shape difference is preserved (those have legitimately different payloads). 8 lines insertion / 16 deletion. `pnpm check` 1037 passed / 7 skipped; `pnpm smoke:broad` 53/53 PASS; `pnpm smoke:live` 9/9 PASS (prior failure cleared).

- observability package monolith split (round 1) — `packages/observability/src/index.ts` 2,060 → 1,525 lines (-535 / -26.0%): extracted the four sliding-window detector / tracker / evaluator classes into a focused module. **`packages/observability/src/observability-detectors.ts`** (567 lines) owns the JARVIS-style alarm primitives — `CostAnomalyDetector` (rolling-window cost monitor that fires when latest exceeds `baseline × thresholdMultiplier` with `windowSize:100`/`thresholdMultiplier:3`/`minSamples:10` defaults), `MonthlyBudgetTracker` (per-tenant USD aggregator with month-rollover reset + bounded `maxTenants:10000` FIFO eviction + ok/warning/exceeded status under `warningPercent:80`), `PromptDriftDetector` (rolling-window first-half / second-half mean-shift detector for input + output lengths with 1% baseline-mean stddev floor when baseline is uniform; default `windowSize:200`/`deviationThreshold:2σ`/`minSamples:20`), `SloAlertEvaluator` (rolling-window P95 latency + error-rate evaluator with per-type cooldown + minimum-sample gating; throws on out-of-range `latencyThresholdMs`/`errorRateThreshold`/`windowSeconds`/`cooldownSeconds`). - reactor-compat-routes.ts split (round 9): the 102-line agent-compat block (`GET /.well-known/agent-card.json` + `/api/admin/agent-specs` CRUD + `/api/admin/models`) extracted into a new `apps/api/src/agent-compat-routes.ts`. 11 helpers (`agentCardResponse`, `toAgentSpecResponse`, `findAgentSpec`, `findAgentSpecOrReply`, `parseAgentSpecInput`, `agentSpecNotFound`, `agentSpecInputError`, `toAgentSpecUpdateInput`, `parseAgentMode`, `isRecord`, `listAdminModelRegistry`) plus `ParseResult` and `ApiError` types promoted to `export`. reactor-compat-routes.ts now 9,694 lines (-946 across the nine split rounds, ~8.9% off the original 10,640 monolith). - reactor-compat-routes.ts split (round 7): the user-memory routes (`GET/PUT(facts|preferences)/DELETE /api/user-memory/:userId` + `POST /api/error-report`) extracted into a new `apps/api/src/user-memory-compat-routes.ts`. 7 helpers (`canAccessUserMemory`, `readUserMemory`, `updateUserMemory`, `deleteUserMemory`, `toUserMemoryResponse`, `userForbidden`, `userMemoryNotFound`) promoted to `export`. The wrapper `registerMemoryAndFeedbackRoutes` collapses to a 3-line dispatcher (registerUserMemoryCompatRoutes + registerFeedbackRoutes). reactor-compat-routes.ts now 9,973 lines (-667 across the seven split rounds, ~6.3% off the original 10,640 monolith — under 10k for the first time and falling). HTTP-verified: GET correctly 403s without auth, POST /api/error-report returns 204.
- Cost attribution wired end-to-end: `recordTokenUsageEvent` in agent-core's model-invocation module now estimates `estimatedCostUsd` via `@muse/cache`'s pricing table, and `recordRunComplete` in the lifecycle module persists the same per-run cost to `AgentRunRecord.costUsd`. Until now both fields stayed at 0 even for known-priced models because no caller ever computed pricing — the cost-anomaly detector + budget tracker (iter 73-75) were silently fed zeros, and `/api/admin/users/usage/{cost,daily,by-model}` always reported `costUsd: 0`. HTTP-verified after a single `openai/gpt-4o-mini` chat: every aggregator now returns the correctly-scaled value (~$0.0000045 for 2 input + 7 output tokens). 4 new direct unit tests cover the priced + unknown-model paths in both modules.
- reactor-compat-routes.ts split (round 6): the 132-line document-routes block (`/api/documents` list/create + `/batch` + `/search` + delete single/bulk with content-hash dedup) extracted into a new `apps/api/src/document-compat-routes.ts` module. 14 more helpers (`createDocument`, `listDocuments`, `searchDocuments`, `deleteDocument`, `deleteDocuments`, `findDocumentByContentHash`, `validateAddDocumentBody`, `duplicateDocumentConflict`, `computeContentHash`, `prefixValidationDetails`, `toDocumentResponse`, `toSearchResultResponse`, `readNumber`, `stringField`, `stringArrayField`, `jsonObjectField`) promoted to `export`. reactor-compat-routes.ts now under 10k for the first time at 10,006 lines (-634 across the six split rounds, ~6% off the original). - RAG HyDE/Decomposition transformers + a default pipeline are now actually wired. The `createLlmHypotheticalDocumentTransformer` and `createLlmDecomposingQueryTransformer` exports had no production caller; new `composeQueryTransformers` (dedup-aware concat), `createDefaultRagQueryTransformer` (env-gated HyDE/Decompose chain), `createDocumentStoreRetriever` (lazy BM25 over `RagDocumentStore`), and `createDefaultRagPipeline` (assembles the full `DefaultRagPipeline`) now compose cleanly. autoconfigure passes the pipeline into `createAgentRuntime` when `MUSE_RAG_PIPELINE_ENABLED=true`; HyDE via `MUSE_RAG_HYDE_ENABLED`, decomposition via `MUSE_RAG_DECOMPOSE_ENABLED` (+ `MUSE_RAG_DECOMPOSE_MAX_QUERIES`). 12 new unit tests cover composition, env-gating, retriever indexing + cache invalidation, and end-to-end pipeline retrieval. HTTP-verified: chat with the flag enabled still completes (empty store → empty context, no-op); baseline path without the flag is unchanged.
- agent-core/index.ts split (round 3): hook orchestration (`invokeHooks`, `hooksForInvocation`, `recordHookTrace`, `hookInvocation`) extracted into a new `hook-orchestration.ts` module. invokeHooks now takes a small deps struct ({hooks, hookRegistry?, hookTraceStore?}) so the runtime collapses to a one-liner. index.ts shrank 1880 → 1788 lines (-92, total -220 across iter 82/83/87). 6 new direct unit tests cover lifecycle dispatch, hook-failure isolation, registry-overrides-static merging, missing-store no-op, and store-error swallowing.
- Slack progress hook is now actually wired: the `createSlackProgressHook` library export from `@muse/integrations` had no production caller. autoconfigure now constructs a `FetchSlackWebApiMessageTransport` and registers the hook on the runtime when `MUSE_SLACK_BOT_TOKEN` is set (env-gated by `MUSE_SLACK_PROGRESS_ENABLED`, default true; throttle tunable via `MUSE_SLACK_PROGRESS_INTERVAL_MS`, default 1500ms). The hook fires `assistant.threads.setStatus` before/after every tool call when the run carries `slackChannelId` + `slackThreadTs` metadata, no-ops otherwise. HTTP-verified: a plan-execute chat with the metadata pair completes cleanly even when the Slack API call fails (fail-open onError); baseline chats without the metadata are unaffected.
- Live-LLM plan-execute coverage strengthened: the existing `pnpm smoke:live` plan-execute check now strictly asserts `toolsUsed.includes("time_now")` and a weekday in the synthesised content when the planner cooperates (status=200), proving the full plan→tool→synth loop fires against real LLMs. A new `/api/chat/stream` plan-execute live check asserts `plan_generated → synthesis_started → done` SSE events fire in order. Same strict plan-execute assertion added to `pnpm smoke:live:all` so every wired provider (Gemini/Anthropic/OpenAI) is covered. Both retain a PLAN_* error fallback for flaky planners so the smoke stays green-friendly.
- Conversation summaries are now operator-editable via HTTP: `GET/PUT/DELETE /api/admin/sessions/:sessionId/summary` exposes the persisted store iter 81 wired into the runtime so operators can inspect, override, or wipe the auto-generated compaction summary. Validates non-empty narrative + non-negative summarizedUpToIndex; returns CONVERSATION_SUMMARY_STORE_UNAVAILABLE when no store is configured. HTTP-verified end-to-end: a 31-turn chat populates the store, GET returns the auto-summary, PUT replaces it with an operator override, DELETE returns 204 and a follow-up GET correctly 404s.
- agent-core/index.ts split (round 2): the resilience + tracing model-call layer (`generateWithTracing`, `generateWithFallback`, `generateWithResilience`, `recordTokenUsageEvent`) extracted into a new `model-invocation.ts` module as a single composed `invokeModel` function (timeout → retry → fallback → circuit-breaker → tracing). index.ts shrank from 1971 → 1880 lines; 8 new direct unit tests cover each resilience layer (retry-then-success, fallback rescue, breaker open after threshold, request timeout, sink failure tracer span). HTTP-verified `muse.model.generate` span + token-usage row still flow end-to-end.
- agent-core/index.ts split (kickoff): the four run-lifecycle recording methods (`recordRunStart`, `recordRunComplete`, `recordCheckpoint`, `recordRunFailure`) extracted into a new `lifecycle.ts` module as standalone fail-open functions taking a small deps struct. AgentRuntime keeps thin wrappers so the runtime call sites are unchanged. 7 new direct unit tests cover the lifecycle module independently of the runtime; HTTP-verified the run/messages/userId/workspaceId path still records correctly end-to-end.
- ConversationSummaryStore is now actually wired into the runtime (was instantiated but unused). AgentRuntime gained two pre/post-run hooks: `applyStoredConversationSummary` prepends a persisted summary as a `[Conversation summary` system message before trim, and `persistConversationSummaryFromRequest` writes the trimmed summary back keyed by `metadata.sessionId` whenever `summaryInserted=true`. Honors the COMPACTION_SUMMARY_PREFIX so trim extends rather than duplicates. Persistence env-gated by `MUSE_CONVERSATION_SUMMARY_PERSIST` (default true). HTTP-verified: a 31-turn conversation with `sessionId="verify-81"` triggers compaction (summaryInserted=true, removedCount=23) and the round-trip second chat with the same sessionId completes without errors; 4 unit tests verify the inject-back path with request spies.
- CLI gained an `orchestrate` command group (`muse orchestrate run|list|get|stats`) covering the full multi-agent surface from iter 70's race-mode work. Run subcommand validates mode + maxWorkers locally and threads workerIds CSV → array. HTTP-verified end-to-end: with two specs registered, `orchestrate run --mode race --workers alpha,beta "Pick one"` returns one winner; `orchestrate stats` reports `byMode.race.runs: 1`.
- Cache provider attribution fixed: `resolveProvider` was only consulting the model-prefix table (gpt-, claude-, gemini-, …), so `/admin/cache.hitsByProvider` always reported `{ unknown: N }` for diagnostic/ollama/openrouter/anthropic-prefixed model strings even when callers specified the provider explicitly via `<provider>/<model>`. Now trusts the structural provider/model prefix first; HTTP-verified `{ diagnostic: 1 }` after a cached chat.
- CLI gained a `jarvis` command group (`muse jarvis runtime|loopback|snapshot`) that surfaces the JARVIS introspection endpoints from iters 63/66 plus the observability dashboard from iters 73-75 directly in the terminal. HTTP-verified end-to-end against a live API: `runtime` shows capabilities/tools, `loopback` lists all 10 ambient MCP servers, `snapshot` returns `latency` + `slo.latencySamples` + `drift.sampleCount` + per-tenant `budgets` after a real chat.
- CLI gained a `specs` command group (`muse specs list`, `muse specs get <name>`, `muse specs resolve <text...>`) so operators can introspect agent-spec routing without curl. Resolve fails fast on empty prompts; HTTP-verified end-to-end against a live diagnostic API: a posted `timekeeper` spec is correctly returned by list/get and resolved by keyword match.
- CLI `chat` command gained a `--mode <react|plan_execute>` flag that threads `metadata.agentMode` through every chat path: local runtime, remote `/api/chat`, and remote `/api/chat/stream`. Unknown values fail fast with a clear error. HTTP-verified: `muse chat --stream --mode plan_execute "What time is it now?"` walks through the full planning → tool-call → synthesis loop end-to-end against a diagnostic API.
- MonthlyBudgetTracker is now wired and per-tenant: a new `createBudgetTrackingTokenUsageSink` chains around the cost-anomaly wrapper and forwards each usage event's `tenantId`/`estimatedCostUsd` to the tracker. `MonthlyBudgetTracker` gained a `tenantIds()` accessor so the snapshot provider can enumerate which tenants to surface; `/api/admin/jarvis/snapshot.budgets` now returns one entry per active tenant with `limitUsd`/`status`/`totalCostUsd`. Limit tunable via `MUSE_BUDGET_MONTHLY_LIMIT_USD` (0 = no limit, status stays "ok").
- Drift detector and cost-anomaly detector are now wired alongside SLO: a generalised `createDerivedAgentMetrics` fans `recordTokenUsage` into `PromptDriftDetector` (input + output token lengths) and a new `createCostAnomalyFeedingTokenUsageSink` fans every recorded usage event into `CostAnomalyDetector`. `/api/admin/jarvis/snapshot.drift` and `.cost` now populate after real runs; `pnpm smoke:broad` asserts `drift.sampleCount > 0` and `cost.baselineUsd` is a number. Thresholds tunable via `MUSE_DRIFT_*` and `MUSE_COST_ANOMALY_*` env vars.
- SLO evaluator is now actually fed: a new `createSloFeedingAgentMetrics` wrapper fans every `recordAgentRun` event into a default-wired `SloAlertEvaluator`, and `/api/admin/jarvis/snapshot.slo` now reports `latencySamples`, `resultSamples`, `errorRate`, and `violations` after real agent runs (was always absent). Thresholds tunable via `MUSE_SLO_LATENCY_THRESHOLD_MS`, `MUSE_SLO_ERROR_RATE_THRESHOLD`, `MUSE_SLO_WINDOW_SECONDS`, `MUSE_SLO_COOLDOWN_SECONDS`, `MUSE_SLO_MIN_SAMPLES`.
- Trace events now actually surface: the in-memory `QueryableTraceEventSink` autoconfigure built was being thrown away instead of exposed on `assembly.observability`, so `/api/admin/traces` and `/api/admin/traces/:traceId/spans` had been silently empty even though the tracer was recording. `pnpm smoke:broad` now asserts at least one `muse.model.generate` span appears after a chat.
- Token usage is now actually recorded: `createAgentRuntime` in autoconfigure was missing the `tokenUsageSink` wire-through, so every `/api/admin/token-cost/*` endpoint and the `tokenCost` slot of `/api/admin/jarvis/snapshot` had been silently empty. Fixed via one-line plumbing plus a `pnpm smoke:broad` upgrade that now asserts `daily`, `top-expensive`, and `by-session?runId=smoke-broad-chat` actually return populated rows after the earlier chat call.
- Multi-agent orchestrator gained a `race` mode that resolves with the first successfully-completing worker (other workers continue in the background but their outcomes are dropped). The HTTP route, history stats `byMode`, and `pnpm smoke:broad` all extend cleanly; `NoAgentWorkerError` still fires when every worker fails.
- DiagnosticModelProvider now also emits a single-step plan calling `time_now` when that tool appears in `[Available Tools]`, so `pnpm smoke:broad` exercises the full plan-execute streaming sequence end-to-end (`plan_generated` → `plan_step_executing` → `plan_step_result` → `synthesis_started` → `done`) without a real LLM.
- DiagnosticModelProvider now recognizes the planning prompt shape and returns `[]`, which makes plan-execute fall back to the direct-answer synthesis path. `pnpm smoke:broad` gained a /chat/stream check that asserts `plan_generated` + `synthesis_started` SSE events fire end-to-end without needing a real LLM, closing the verification gap from iteration #64.
- `createLoopbackMcpToolsFromEnv` lets operators plug the JARVIS ambient toolset purely via env: `MUSE_LOOPBACK_MCP_ENABLED=true` registers the eight default loopback servers as namespaced Muse tools (`muse.time.now`, `muse.fs.read`, …); `MUSE_LOOPBACK_FETCH_HOSTS` and `MUSE_LOOPBACK_FS_ROOTS` add the opt-in fetch and fs servers when their allowlists are supplied. HTTP-verified: tool count jumps from 10 → 32 with the env flags set.
- `GET /api/jarvis/loopback` exposes the built-in MCP loopback catalog (8 default servers + 2 opt-in) with tool names, risk, opt-in flag, and env-hint requirements so any operator or chat surface can discover what JARVIS-style ambient tools are pluggable without reading source.
- `createFilesystemMcpServer` adds an opt-in, allowlist-rooted, read-only filesystem loopback MCP server (read/list/stat) for JARVIS-style workspace inspection without giving the agent free disk access. Path resolution rejects sibling-prefix collisions (`/etc` ≠ `/etc-passwd`) and `..` traversal.
- Plan-execute now streams `plan-generated`, `plan-step-executing`, `plan-step-result`, and `synthesis-started` events so SSE consumers can render reasoning progress; `executePlanExecuteLoop` drains a single `streamPlanExecute` generator (one source of truth for streaming and non-streaming paths).
- `GET /api/jarvis/runtime` exposes a public manifest (capabilities, locales, tool risk counts, agent-spec/setting totals) so any chat surface or automation can introspect the conductor without admin auth or secrets.

  implementations instead of route-local state when the runtime assembly provides a database handle.
- Reactor-compatible conversation summaries now use a shared memory-layer `ConversationSummaryStore` with

  Slack activity, tenant quality/tools/quota CSV exports, audit CSV export, and task-memory maintenance.

- The broad `/api/admin/*` compatibility fallback was removed so unmapped admin routes fail with 404 instead of
  pretending to be migrated.
- Slack FAQ admin compatibility now matches Reactor response envelopes for registration lists, stats, events,
  feedback snapshots, and channel deletion.
- Input Guard audit compatibility now records settings/simulate operations and returns the Reactor `{ audits, total }`
  envelope instead of a static empty response.
